Understanding as Intentional Attention in Wad'
Al-Attar and Abd al-Hakim explain that 'understanding' in the definition of wad' means intentional attention, resolving the problem of simultaneous attention to two things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the concept of 'intentional attention' (iltifat qasdi) resolves the problem of attending to two things simultaneously when understanding wad'.

Core Idea
Understanding in wad' is intentional attention, not full knowledge, so the mind attends to the word, and the meaning follows without simultaneous awareness.

In this lesson, we delve deeper into what 'understanding' means in the definition of wad'. Al-Attar and Abd al-Hakim clarify that the understanding is a form of intentional attention (iltifat qasdi). This subtle distinction resolves a potential paradox: how can one attend to both the word and its meaning at the same moment? The answer lies in the sequential nature of understanding.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem of simultaneous attention
If understanding both the placed thing and its meaning requires active attention, then one would need to attend to two things at the same moment, which is cognitively impossible.
This is a classic objection against any definition that requires simultaneous awareness.
2
Identify the proposed solution: intentional attention
Al-Attar explains that 'understanding' in the definition means 'intentional attention' (iltifat qasdi). The mind intentionally attends to the first thing (the word), and the second (the meaning) follows as a necessary concomitant without requiring separate attention.
The term used is 'isti'qab' (following), indicating a sequential process.
3
Understand the notion of concomitant (lazim)
The word and its meaning are related as necessary concomitant. When the mind brings the word to attention, the meaning comes to mind automatically as a result, not as a separate act of attention.
4
Appreciate Abd al-Hakim's reinforcement
Abd al-Hakim adds that no one doubts that when a word is used, the mind attends to it, and the attention to the meaning is a second, distinct moment. Thus, there is no simultaneity.
This resolves the objection definitively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْوَضْعُ : جَعْلُ الشَّيْءِ بإزاء آخَرَ ، بحيثُ إذا فُهِمَ الأَوَّل ؛ فُهِمَ الثَّاني. الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : وَالْوَضْعُ) أي : ومطلق الوضع؛ كان وضع لفظ أو وضع غيره، فهو تعريف لمطلق الوضع؛ لا لوضع اللفظ ؛ إذْ هو جعل اللفظ بإزاء المعنى، فقوله: (جعل الشَّيء)؛ أي : لفظاً كان أو غيره، وقوله : (بإزاء) أي : بمقابلة آخر، وهو الموضوع له . وقوله : (بحيث إذا فهم الأول)؛ أي: بحيث إذا أُدرك الأوَّلُ وهو الموضوع؛ أي : وعُلِمَ وضعُهُ لِلشَّيءِ الَّذي جُعِلَ بإزائه، وقوله: (فهم الثاني)؛ أي: وهو الموضوع له ، واعترض بأنَّ «إذا» للإهمال، فتكون القضيَّةُ معها في حكم الجزئية، فتقتضي أَنَّهُ إذا فُهِمَ الأَوَّلُ ؛ يُفْهَمُ الثَّاني تارةً، وتارةٌ لا يُفهم معَ أَنَّهُ لا بُدَّ في الوضع مِن فَهُم الثَّاني عند فهم الأوَّلِ في جميع الأحوال والأوقات، فكان المناسبُ إبدال إذا بـ «كُلَّما»؛ الَّتي هي من سور الإيجاب الكُلِّيِّ، فتأمل. (قَوْلُهُ : إِذَا فُهِمَ الْأَوَّلُ ؛ فُهِمَ الثَّانِي) أي : مع العِلْمِ بالوضع. العطار (قَوْلُهُ: وَالْوَضْعُ جَعْلُ الشَّيْءٍ) عدل عن اللَّفْظِ للعموم في سائر الأوضاع، وأمَّا وَضْعُ اللَّفظِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ يَنقَسِمُ إلى شَخصيّ ونَوعِيٌّ، وكُلُّ مِنهُما ينقسم إلى ثلاثة أقسامٍ؛ بيَّنَّاهَا غايةَ البيانِ في حواشِي شَرْحِ العِصَامِ على الوضعيَّةِ. (قَوْلُهُ : بِحَيْثُ إِذَا فُهِمَ الْأَوَّلُ ، فُهِمَ الثَّانِي) أي: عُلِمَ ، والعِلْمُ في الموضعَيْنِ بمعنى الالتفاتِ القصدي؛ إذْ لا ينتقلُ الدّهنُ مِن حضورِ اللَّفْظِ تبعاً إلى المعنى المطابقيّ، وَلَا مِنَ المعنَى المطابقي الحاصل تبعاً إلى المعنى الالتزامي؛ لأنَّ إحضار الملزومِ شَرْطٌ في الانتقال إلى اللَّازِمِ ، وَأَنَّ المراد باللُّزوم؛ الاستعقاب، فَلَا يردُ لزوم الالتفات إلى شَيئين في آن واحِدٍ، ولا يصح الجواب بأنَّه يجوز أن يكون الالتفات إلى أحدِهِما بالإحضار ؛ وإلى الآخَرِ بِالتَّبِعِ، وَمَا قِيْلَ إِنَّهُ يُشْكِلُ بما إذا كان المعنى مُلتفتاً إليه لأنَّه يلزم الالتفات إلى الملتفت إليه ؛ فَوَهُم، إذ لا يَشُكُ أحدٌ في أَنَّهُ كُلَّمَا اللفظ الموضوع لمعنى ؛ يلتفتُ الذَّهنُ إليه، والالتفاتُ الثَّاني غيرُ الأَوَّلِ، ا.هـ. عبد الحكيم، وبه تعلمُ مَا قِيْلَ هُنَا . شمع
And convention (wad') is: placing a thing in correspondence with another, such that when the first is understood, the second is understood. (Al-Dasuqi: His saying: 'and convention' means absolute convention, whether it is the convention of a word or something else. So it is a definition of absolute convention, not of the convention of a word, since the latter is placing a word in correspondence with a meaning. So his saying: 'placing the thing' means whether it is a word or something else. His saying: 'in correspondence with' means opposite to another, which is the thing for which it is placed. His saying: 'such that when the first is understood' means such that when the first—which is the placed thing—is perceived, and its placement for the thing in whose correspondence it was placed is known. His saying: 'the second is understood' means the thing for which it is placed. An objection is raised that 'idha' (when) is for [occasional] affirmation, making the proposition particular, implying that when the first is understood, the second is understood sometimes and sometimes not, whereas in convention, the second must be understood upon understanding the first in all cases and times. So it would be appropriate to replace 'idha' with 'kullama' (whenever), which is a quantifier of universal affirmation. Ponder. His saying: 'when the first is understood, the second is understood' means with knowledge of the convention. (Al-Attar: His saying: 'and convention is placing the thing' he turned away from 'word' to achieve generality for all conventions. As for the convention of a word, it divides into personal and generic, and each of them divides into three types, which we have explained thoroughly in the glosses on the commentary of al-‘Isam on al-Wad‘iyya. His saying: 'such that when the first is understood, the second is understood' means known, and knowledge in both places means intentional attention; because the mind does not transition from the presence of the word concomitantly to the meaning by correspondence, nor from the meaning by correspondence obtained concomitantly to the implicational meaning, because bringing the necessary is a condition for transitioning to the necessary. And that the intended meaning of 'concomitance' is 'following', so the objection of necessary attention to two things at one moment does not arise. Nor is the answer correct that it is permissible for attention to one of them to be by presentation and to the other by concomitance. And what is said that it is problematic when the meaning is attended to because it would necessitate attention to that which is attended to is a mistake, since no one doubts that whenever a word is placed for a meaning, the mind attends to it, and the second attention is other than the first. End of Abd al-Hakim's statement. By this you know what is said here. Sham‘)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage defines wad' (convention) as a general concept. The core definition: placing a thing in correspondence with another such that understanding the first leads to understanding the second. Al-Dasuqi clarifies that this is absolute convention, not limited to words, so it covers any kind of conventional relation. The definition uses 'idha' (when), which an objector argues is a particle for occasional cases, making the proposition particular, whereas convention requires universal understanding (whenever the first is known, the second is understood). The commentator suggests replacing it with 'kullama' (whenever) to indicate universal affirmation. Al-Attar further explains that the definition deliberately uses 'thing' instead of 'word' for generality. He then discusses the types of verbal convention. The key technical point: the 'understanding' here means intentional attention, not full knowledge. This avoids the problem of attending to two things simultaneously, because the transition from the placed thing (word) to the meaning is successive, not simultaneous. Abd al-Hakim elaborates that the mind does not hold both at once; rather, one is attended to intentionally and the other follows. The passage ends with a note that this explanation resolves the difficulty.

Key Terms

موضوع له
لازم
استعقاب

Key Takeaway
Understanding in wad' is intentional attention, not full knowledge, allowing the mind to attend to the word first, and then the meaning follows sequentially, avoiding the problem of simultaneity.

Defining Dalaalat al-Tadammun: Signification by Inclusion
Author defines dalaalat al-tadammun and contrasts it with other significations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define dalaalat al-tadammun and distinguish it from dalaalat al-mutabaqa and dalaalat al-iltizam using the example of 'insan'.

Core Idea
Dalaalat al-tadammun is a single understanding of a part within the whole, without sequential transition.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational concept of dalaalat al-tadammun (signification by inclusion). The author defines it as a word's signification upon a part of its meaning, and the commentator Dasuqi clarifies that this is a simultaneous grasp of the whole and its part. Understanding this distinction is crucial for analyzing how words convey their meanings in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate 'دلالة التضمن' in the Arabic and note that it is the definiendum. The definition is given as 'دلالته على جزئه' i.e., its signification upon its part.
The 'part' refers to a part of the meaning for which the word was placed.
2
Extract the definition from the commentary
Dasuqi explains that this signification occurs 'في حال دلالته على الكل' i.e., in the state of signifying the whole, not separately. So tadammun is understanding a part within the whole meaning.
This contrasts with a separate signification of the part alone.
3
Distinguish tadammun from mutabaqa and iltizam
Mutabaqa is signification of the word for its entire meaning (e.g., 'insan' for 'rational animal'), while tadammun is for a part (e.g., 'insan' for 'animal' only). Iltizam involves a necessary implication outside the original meaning and requires mental transition, whereas tadammun does not.
The passage explicitly contrasts tadammun with iltizam regarding transition.
4
Apply the definition to a concrete example
Using the example from the text: when you say 'insan', its mutabaqa is upon 'hayawan natiq', and its tadammun is upon either 'hayawan' or 'natiq'. Verify that the part is understood within the whole.
This example shows the practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في تعريفِ الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ وأحكامها. دَلَالَةُ التَضَمُنِ) (ق) دلالته عَلَى جُزْئِهِ)؛ أي جزء المعنى الموضوع له. الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : وَدَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى جُزْئِهِ ) أي : في حالِ دلالتِهِ على الكلِّ ؛ لا في حالةٍ أُخرى، فالتَّضمُّنُ فَهُمُ الجزء في ضمن الكلِّ ، وَلَا شكٍّ أنَّهُ إذا فهم المعنى ؛ فهمت ه معه، فليس في دلالةِ التَّضمن انتقال من اللَّفظِ إلى المعنى، ومن المعنى إلى الجزء، بل هو فَهم واحد يُسمَّى بالقياس إلى تمام المعنى مطابقة، وبالقياس إلى جزئه تضمناً، بخلافِ دلالةِ الالتزام، فإنَّه لا بُدَّ فيها من الانتقالِ مِنَ اللّفظ للمعنى، وَمِنَ المعنى إلى اللازم ؛ ضرورة أنَّ اللَّازِمَ لا دخل لهُ في الوضعِ وهذا وجهُ مَن يقولُ : إِنَّ التَّضمُنيَّةَ وضعيّة، والالتزاميَّةَ عقليَّةٌ، وذهبَ بعضُهم إلى أنَّ في دلالةِ التَّضمُّنِ انتقالاً من اللفظ إلى المعنى إجمالاً، ثم إلى أجزائه تفصيلاً، وبحث فيه بأنَّهُ يستلزم تقدُّم وجودِ الكلِّ على وجودِ الجزء في الذهنِ، مَعَ اتَّفَاقِهِم على تقدم الجزء على الكلِّ في الوجودَيْنِ ؛ الذهني والخارجي، وبأنَّهُ يستلزمُ فَهُم الجزء مرَّتين ؛ مرَّةً في ضمن المركَّب، وأخرَى مُنفرداً. والوجدان يكذِّبُه ، فَالأقيس : ما ذهب إليه بعضُهم من أنَّ التَّضِمُّنَ؛ فَهُمُ الجزء في ضمن الكلِّ ؛ لا بعد فهمه ، وقد يُجاب عن البحث الأوَّلِ بأَنَّ تقدُّمَ الجزء على الكلِّ في الوجودين؛ محله إذا اعتبر فَهم الكلِّ بوجه لا من اللفظ، وأمَّا إذا اعتبر فهمه من اللّفظ الذي وضعَ لِلكلِّ، ولم يوضع للجزء ؛ فلا نسلّم تقدُّم الجزء، كيف وهو مخالف لوضع اللفظ للكلِّ؟!، وأيضاً فهم الكلِّ من اللفظ إِنَّما هو فَهم إجمالي . والجزء لا يتقدَّمُ إلا على الفَهْمِ التّفصيلي، ولذا قالُوا : إِنَّ النَّوعَ قد يحضر في الذهن، وَلَا يحضر الجنس ، يعنون بحضورِ النَّوع ؛ الحضور الإجماليَّ لَا التَّفصيلي. (قَوْلُهُ : وَدَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى جُزْئِهِ تَضَمُّنُ ... إلخ) حاصلُهُ أَنَّكَ إِذا قُلْتَ: إنسان؛ فدلالته على الحيوانِ النَّاطِقِ مُطابقة، ودلالته على أحدهما تَضَمُّن . (قَوْلُهُ : أَيْ: جُزْءِ الْمَعْنَى الْمَوْضُوع لَهُ أي: حيث كان المعنى الموضوع له. العطار (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى جُزْئِهِ قِيلَ : وإِنْ لمْ يُعْلَمُ ذلكَ الجزء بعينه، كما إذا عُلِمَ أَنَّ اللَّفْظَ الكُل موضوع لِشَيءٍ مُعيَّن وغيرِهِ ولم يعيَّن ذلك الغيرُ بعينه، وهو مفهوم في ضمن. (تَضَمُّنُ) لكون الجزء في ضمن المعنى الموضوع له كـ: (دلالة الإنسان على الحيوانِ أو النَّاطِقِ . الدسوقي مركَّباً كـ (حيوان) ناطق، الذي وضع له إنسان، فدلالة التضمنِ إِنَّمَا تكونُ فيما لهُ جزء، وهو المعنى المركَّبُ ؛ بخلافِ الدَّلالةِ المطابقيَّة، فإنَّها تكون في ذلك وفيما لا جزء له ؛ كالنُّقطة والجوهر الفرد، فتكون المطابقيَّةُ أعمَّ مِنَ التَّضمنيَّة عموماً مطلقاً، وقولُهُ: (تَضَمُّن)؛ أي: تُسمَّى تَضمَّناً ؛ أي: دلالةً تضمن. (قَوْلُهُ : لِكَوْنِ الْجُزْء... إلخ) عِلَّةٌ لِتَسميتها تَضمُّنيَّة، وقوله: (كَدلالة الإنسان)؛ أي : كدلالة لفظ الإنسان الموضوع للحيوانِ النَّاطِقِ في حال إطلاقه على ذلك.
Chapter: On the definition of the three significations and their rulings. The signification of inclusion: its signification upon its part; i.e., part of the meaning placed. Dasuqi: His statement: 'And its signification upon its part' means in the state of its signification upon the whole, not in another state. So inclusion is the understanding of the part within the whole, and there is no doubt that when the meaning is understood, it is understood with it. So in signification of inclusion there is no transition from the word to the meaning and from the meaning to the part, but it is a single understanding called, in relation to the complete meaning, correspondence, and in relation to its part, inclusion, unlike signification of implication, for it necessarily involves transition from the word to the meaning and from the meaning to the necessary, because the necessary has no role in the placement. This is the view of those who say that inclusion is conventional and implication is rational. Some went to the view that in signification of inclusion there is a transition from the word to the meaning summarily, then to its parts in detail. It was discussed that this requires the whole's existence to precede the part's existence in the mind, despite their agreement on the part's priority over the whole in both mental and external existence, and that it requires understanding the part twice: once within the compound and once alone. And intuition belies it. So the sounder is what some went to: that inclusion is understanding the part within the whole, not after understanding it. The first discussion may be answered by saying that the priority of the part over the whole in the two existences applies when the understanding of the whole is considered in a manner not from the word. But when considered from the word placed for the whole and not placed for the part, we do not concede the priority of the part. How can it be when it contradicts the placement of the word for the whole? Also, understanding the whole from the word is only a summary understanding. The part is prior only to detailed understanding. Hence they said that the species may be present in the mind while the genus is not present, meaning by presence of the species the summary presence, not the detailed. (His statement: 'And its signification upon its part is inclusion, etc.') Its gist is that if you say 'human,' its signification upon 'rational animal' is correspondence, and its signification upon either of them is inclusion. (His statement: 'i.e., part of the meaning placed') i.e., since the meaning placed. Attar: (His statement: 'upon its part') it was said: even if that part is not known specifically, as when it is known that the whole word is placed for something specific and something else without that something else being specified, and it is a concept within. (Inclusion) because the part is within the meaning placed for it, like: (the signification of 'human' upon 'animal' or 'rational'). Dasuqi: Compound like 'rational animal' for which 'human' is placed. So signification of inclusion only exists for what has a part, which is the compound meaning; unlike signification of correspondence, for it exists in that and in what has no part, like the point and the simple substance. So correspondence is more general than inclusion absolutely. His statement: (Inclusion) means it is called inclusion, i.e., signification of inclusion. (His statement: 'Because the part... etc.') is the cause for its being called inclusion. His statement: (like the signification of 'human') i.e., like the signification of the word 'human' placed for 'rational animal' in the state of its being used for that.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage defines dalaalat al-tadammun (signification by inclusion) and discusses its nature. The author begins by stating the definition: it is the signification of a word for a part of its meaning. The commentator Dasuqi explains that this signification occurs in the context of signifying the whole, not separately. He clarifies that tadammun is a single act of understanding that simultaneously grasps the whole and its part. In contrast to dalaalat al-iltizam (implicative signification), tadammun does not require a transition from the word to the meaning to the implication. Some scholars argue that tadammun involves a transition from the word to the whole meaning summarily, then to its parts in detail. However, this view is criticized for implying a temporal priority of the whole over the part in the mind, contradicting the agreed priority of part over whole. The correct view is that tadammun is simply understanding the part within the whole, not after understanding it. An objection is answered: when understanding from a word placed for the whole, the part does not precede because the understanding is summary. The passage uses the example of 'insan' (human) signifying 'hayawan natiq' (rational animal) by mutabaqa, and signifying either 'hayawan' or 'natiq' by tadammun. Finally, Dasuqi clarifies that tadammun only applies to composite meanings, whereas mutabaqa applies to both composite and simple meanings, making mutabaqa more general.

Key Terms
دلالة التضمن
دلالة المطابقة
تضمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does dalaalat al-tadammun differ from dalaalat al-iltizam?
A) Tadammun requires a transition from word to meaning to part, while iltizam does not.
B) Tadammun is a single understanding without transition, while iltizam requires a transition from word to meaning to implication.
C) Tadammun is only for composite meanings, while iltizam is for simple meanings.
D) Tadammun is a rational signification, while iltizam is conventional.

Key Takeaway
Dalaalat al-tadammun is the simultaneous understanding of a part within the whole meaning, with no mental transition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which type of signification (mutabaqa, tadammun, or iltizam) is involved in the following: the word 'زكاة' (zakat) signifies both 'obligatory charity' and 'the specific portion of wealth.' Justify your answer using the definitions from this lesson.
?
Using the example of 'insan' from the text, construct a sentence in Arabic that demonstrates tadammun, and explain which part is signified by inclusion.

The Debate: Does Tadammun Involve Mental Transition?
Author discusses whether tadammun involves mental transition and presents objections and responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the argument against mental transition in tadammun and evaluate the counterargument using the priority of part over whole.

Core Idea
Tadammun is understanding the part within the whole, not after it; the priority of part over whole applies only to detailed understanding.

Having defined dalaalat al-tadammun, we now examine a key debate: does it involve a mental transition from whole to part? Some scholars argued it does, but the text refutes this by showing that such transition would violate the logical priority of the part over the whole. Understanding this nuance deepens our grasp of signification in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
Find where the text says 'ذهب بعضهم' (some went to) and 'الأقيس' (the sounder). The first view claims tadammun involves transition from word to whole summarily, then to parts in detail. The second says it is simply understanding the part within the whole.
The phrase 'فهم الجزء في ضمن الكل' is central.
2
Extract the objections against the transition view
The text gives two objections: (1) It requires the whole to exist before the part in the mind, but the part is agreed to be prior in both mental and external existence. (2) It would require understanding the part twice: once within the whole and once separately, which intuition ('الوجدان') denies.
These are logical and experiential arguments.
3
Analyze the response to the first objection
The response distinguishes between understanding the whole 'من اللفظ' (from the word) and understanding it otherwise. When understood from a word placed for the whole, the part is not prior because that understanding is summary ('إجمالي'), not detailed. The part is only prior to detailed understanding.
This answer saves the position by specifying the mode of understanding.
4
Assess the conclusion
The text concludes that the sounder view is 'فهم الجزء في ضمن الكل لا بعد فهمه' (understanding the part within the whole, not after understanding it). Thus, tadammun does not involve a real transition.
This is the majority position in Islamic logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في تعريفِ الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ وأحكامها. دَلَالَةُ التَضَمُنِ) (ق) دلالته عَلَى جُزْئِهِ)؛ أي جزء المعنى الموضوع له. الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : وَدَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى جُزْئِهِ ) أي : في حالِ دلالتِهِ على الكلِّ ؛ لا في حالةٍ أُخرى، فالتَّضمُّنُ فَهُمُ الجزء في ضمن الكلِّ ، وَلَا شكٍّ أنَّهُ إذا فهم المعنى ؛ فهمت ه معه، فليس في دلالةِ التَّضمن انتقال من اللَّفظِ إلى المعنى، ومن المعنى إلى الجزء، بل هو فَهم واحد يُسمَّى بالقياس إلى تمام المعنى مطابقة، وبالقياس إلى جزئه تضمناً، بخلافِ دلالةِ الالتزام، فإنَّه لا بُدَّ فيها من الانتقالِ مِنَ اللّفظ للمعنى، وَمِنَ المعنى إلى اللازم ؛ ضرورة أنَّ اللَّازِمَ لا دخل لهُ في الوضعِ وهذا وجهُ مَن يقولُ : إِنَّ التَّضمُنيَّةَ وضعيّة، والالتزاميَّةَ عقليَّةٌ، وذهبَ بعضُهم إلى أنَّ في دلالةِ التَّضمُّنِ انتقالاً من اللفظ إلى المعنى إجمالاً، ثم إلى أجزائه تفصيلاً، وبحث فيه بأنَّهُ يستلزم تقدُّم وجودِ الكلِّ على وجودِ الجزء في الذهنِ، مَعَ اتَّفَاقِهِم على تقدم الجزء على الكلِّ في الوجودَيْنِ ؛ الذهني والخارجي، وبأنَّهُ يستلزمُ فَهُم الجزء مرَّتين ؛ مرَّةً في ضمن المركَّب، وأخرَى مُنفرداً. والوجدان يكذِّبُه ، فَالأقيس : ما ذهب إليه بعضُهم من أنَّ التَّضِمُّنَ؛ فَهُمُ الجزء في ضمن الكلِّ ؛ لا بعد فهمه ، وقد يُجاب عن البحث الأوَّلِ بأَنَّ تقدُّمَ الجزء على الكلِّ في الوجودين؛ محله إذا اعتبر فَهم الكلِّ بوجه لا من اللفظ، وأمَّا إذا اعتبر فهمه من اللّفظ الذي وضعَ لِلكلِّ، ولم يوضع للجزء ؛ فلا نسلّم تقدُّم الجزء، كيف وهو مخالف لوضع اللفظ للكلِّ؟!، وأيضاً فهم الكلِّ من اللفظ إِنَّما هو فَهم إجمالي . والجزء لا يتقدَّمُ إلا على الفَهْمِ التّفصيلي، ولذا قالُوا : إِنَّ النَّوعَ قد يحضر في الذهن، وَلَا يحضر الجنس ، يعنون بحضورِ النَّوع ؛ الحضور الإجماليَّ لَا التَّفصيلي. (قَوْلُهُ : وَدَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى جُزْئِهِ تَضَمُّنُ ... إلخ) حاصلُهُ أَنَّكَ إِذا قُلْتَ: إنسان؛ فدلالته على الحيوانِ النَّاطِقِ مُطابقة، ودلالته على أحدهما تَضَمُّن . (قَوْلُهُ : أَيْ: جُزْءِ الْمَعْنَى الْمَوْضُوع لَهُ أي: حيث كان المعنى الموضوع له. العطار (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى جُزْئِهِ قِيلَ : وإِنْ لمْ يُعْلَمُ ذلكَ الجزء بعينه، كما إذا عُلِمَ أَنَّ اللَّفْظَ الكُل موضوع لِشَيءٍ مُعيَّن وغيرِهِ ولم يعيَّن ذلك الغيرُ بعينه، وهو مفهوم في ضمن. (تَضَمُّنُ) لكون الجزء في ضمن المعنى الموضوع له كـ: (دلالة الإنسان على الحيوانِ أو النَّاطِقِ . الدسوقي مركَّباً كـ (حيوان) ناطق، الذي وضع له إنسان، فدلالة التضمنِ إِنَّمَا تكونُ فيما لهُ جزء، وهو المعنى المركَّبُ ؛ بخلافِ الدَّلالةِ المطابقيَّة، فإنَّها تكون في ذلك وفيما لا جزء له ؛ كالنُّقطة والجوهر الفرد، فتكون المطابقيَّةُ أعمَّ مِنَ التَّضمنيَّة عموماً مطلقاً، وقولُهُ: (تَضَمُّن)؛ أي: تُسمَّى تَضمَّناً ؛ أي: دلالةً تضمن. (قَوْلُهُ : لِكَوْنِ الْجُزْء... إلخ) عِلَّةٌ لِتَسميتها تَضمُّنيَّة، وقوله: (كَدلالة الإنسان)؛ أي : كدلالة لفظ الإنسان الموضوع للحيوانِ النَّاطِقِ في حال إطلاقه على ذلك.
Chapter: On the definition of the three significations and their rulings. The signification of inclusion: its signification upon its part; i.e., part of the meaning placed. Dasuqi: His statement: 'And its signification upon its part' means in the state of its signification upon the whole, not in another state. So inclusion is the understanding of the part within the whole, and there is no doubt that when the meaning is understood, it is understood with it. So in signification of inclusion there is no transition from the word to the meaning and from the meaning to the part, but it is a single understanding called, in relation to the complete meaning, correspondence, and in relation to its part, inclusion, unlike signification of implication, for it necessarily involves transition from the word to the meaning and from the meaning to the necessary, because the necessary has no role in the placement. This is the view of those who say that inclusion is conventional and implication is rational. Some went to the view that in signification of inclusion there is a transition from the word to the meaning summarily, then to its parts in detail. It was discussed that this requires the whole's existence to precede the part's existence in the mind, despite their agreement on the part's priority over the whole in both mental and external existence, and that it requires understanding the part twice: once within the compound and once alone. And intuition belies it. So the sounder is what some went to: that inclusion is understanding the part within the whole, not after understanding it. The first discussion may be answered by saying that the priority of the part over the whole in the two existences applies when the understanding of the whole is considered in a manner not from the word. But when considered from the word placed for the whole and not placed for the part, we do not concede the priority of the part. How can it be when it contradicts the placement of the word for the whole? Also, understanding the whole from the word is only a summary understanding. The part is prior only to detailed understanding. Hence they said that the species may be present in the mind while the genus is not present, meaning by presence of the species the summary presence, not the detailed. (His statement: 'And its signification upon its part is inclusion, etc.') Its gist is that if you say 'human,' its signification upon 'rational animal' is correspondence, and its signification upon either of them is inclusion. (His statement: 'i.e., part of the meaning placed') i.e., since the meaning placed. Attar: (His statement: 'upon its part') it was said: even if that part is not known specifically, as when it is known that the whole word is placed for something specific and something else without that something else being specified, and it is a concept within. (Inclusion) because the part is within the meaning placed for it, like: (the signification of 'human' upon 'animal' or 'rational'). Dasuqi: Compound like 'rational animal' for which 'human' is placed. So signification of inclusion only exists for what has a part, which is the compound meaning; unlike signification of correspondence, for it exists in that and in what has no part, like the point and the simple substance. So correspondence is more general than inclusion absolutely. His statement: (Inclusion) means it is called inclusion, i.e., signification of inclusion. (His statement: 'Because the part... etc.') is the cause for its being called inclusion. His statement: (like the signification of 'human') i.e., like the signification of the word 'human' placed for 'rational animal' in the state of its being used for that.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage defines dalaalat al-tadammun (signification by inclusion) and discusses its nature. The author begins by stating the definition: it is the signification of a word for a part of its meaning. The commentator Dasuqi explains that this signification occurs in the context of signifying the whole, not separately. He clarifies that tadammun is a single act of understanding that simultaneously grasps the whole and its part. In contrast to dalaalat al-iltizam (implicative signification), tadammun does not require a transition from the word to the meaning to the implication. Some scholars argue that tadammun involves a transition from the word to the whole meaning summarily, then to its parts in detail. However, this view is criticized for implying a temporal priority of the whole over the part in the mind, contradicting the agreed priority of part over whole. The correct view is that tadammun is simply understanding the part within the whole, not after understanding it. An objection is answered: when understanding from a word placed for the whole, the part does not precede because the understanding is summary. The passage uses the example of 'insan' (human) signifying 'hayawan natiq' (rational animal) by mutabaqa, and signifying either 'hayawan' or 'natiq' by tadammun. Finally, Dasuqi clarifies that tadammun only applies to composite meanings, whereas mutabaqa applies to both composite and simple meanings, making mutabaqa more general.

Key Terms
تقدم
وجود ذهني
فهم إجمالي
فهم تفصيلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason why the view that tadammun involves transition is rejected?
A) It contradicts the definition of mutabaqa.
B) It requires the whole to precede the part in the mind, but the part is generally agreed to be prior.
C) It is not supported by any recognized scholar.
D) It applies only to simple meanings, not composite ones.

Key Takeaway
Tadammun does not involve mental transition; it is a single, simultaneous understanding of the part within the whole, supported by logical priority arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the statement: 'The word 'عالم' signifies the created universe.' Explain how the transition debate applies to understanding 'عالم' as signifying both the whole universe and its parts (e.g., heavens, earth). Which view from the passage do you support and why?

Definition and Conditions of Dalaalat al-Iltizam
Author defines dalaalat al-iltizam and discusses its condition of necessity (luzum).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of dalaalat al-iltizam and explain why luzum is a condition rather than a differentia.

Core Idea
Implication requires necessary entailment, not just any external relation.

This lesson examines dalaalat al-iltizam (signification by implication). The passage defines it as signification of a word for something external to its placed meaning that necessarily follows. The commentator al-Dasuqi stresses that this necessity (luzum) is a condition, not a differentia, preserving the rational division of signification. The author also critiques a previous claim about composite meanings, reinforcing the wisdom of the assigner (wadi').

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate 'dalaalat al-iltizam' in the Arabic and note its basic description: signification upon what is external to the placed meaning with implication (iltizam).
2
Extract the core definition
The definition is: signification of a word for something external to its placed meaning, but that something must necessarily accompany the primary meaning (luzum). Without luzum, it is not iltizam.
Necessity can be rational ('aqlan) or customary ('urfan).
3
Distinguish iltizam from mutabaqa
The passage explains that if the external meaning were the whole composite, it would be mutabaqa. In iltizam, the external meaning is a single part or attribute that is necessarily linked, not the whole combination.
Example: 'insan' implies 'natiq' by iltizam? Actually tadammun; careful.
4
Understand why luzum is a condition, not a differentia
If luzum were part of the definition (differentia), any external relation would count as iltizam. By making it a condition, the division of signification into three types (mutabaqa, tadammun, iltizam) remains rationally exhaustive.
Al-Jalal al-Dawwani adds: if implication were inside the concept, the condition would be redundant.
5
Recognize the author's critique
The author rejects a view that a word can be placed for a composite meaning with an unspecified part. This would go against the wisdom of the wadi' and the purpose of language (ifada and istifada).
This critique reinforces that definitions must be clear and complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دلالة الالتزام (وَ) دلالته (عَلَى الْخَارج عن المعنى الموضوع له التزام)؛ له ) الدسوقي: (قوله: على الخارج أي: على الخارج عن الموضوع له اللازم له؛ لأن اللزوم شرط في تحقق الالتزامية، وقوله: (التزام)؛ أي: تسمى التزاماً؛ أي: دلالة التزام. العطار: المطابقي؛ فتدبر. ا.هـ. أقول: تدبرناه فوجدناه غير معقول، فإن الدلالة متفرعة على الوضع، وبعد العلم بأن هذا اللفظ موضوع لهذا المعنى المركب، ومعلوم ارتباط أحد الجزأين بالآخر، كيف يقال ما ذكر والواضع حكيم؟ فكيف يضع لفظاً لمعنى مركب؛ جزؤه الثاني غير معين يوجب تعيين الموضوع له حالة الوضع؟ وأيضاً هذا مناف لغرض وضع الألفاظ، وهو إفادة المعاني واستفادتها. (قوله: على الحيوان أو الناطق أي دلالته على واحد من هذين على انفراده؛ لا على المجموع، وإلا؛ كان مطابقة، ولذلك عطف بأو. (قوله: وعلى الخارج) لم يقيده باللازم، وقال بعده: ولا بد من اللزوم عقلاً أو عرفاً... إلخ؛ تنبيهاً على أن اللزوم شرط لتحقق الدلالة الالتزامية؛ لا فصل، فلا يبطل كون حصر الدلالة في الثلاث عقلياً بتجويز دلالته على خارج غير لازم، زاد الجلال الدواني: ولو دخل في مفهومه؛ لغا الاشتراط، قاله بعض الحواشي.
Signification of implication: (And) its signification (upon what is external to the placed meaning is implication) for it. Dasuqi: (His statement: upon what is external) i.e., external to the placed meaning that is necessary for it; because necessity is a condition for the realization of implicative signification. And his statement: (implication) i.e., it is called implication; i.e., signification of implication. Attar: The correspondence; so reflect. End. I say: We reflected upon it and found it unintelligible. For signification is derived from placement, and after knowing that this word is placed for this composite meaning, and the connection of one part to the other is known, how can what was mentioned be said while the assigner is wise? How can he place a word for a composite meaning whose second part is unspecified, while specification of the placed meaning is required at the time of placement? Also, this contradicts the purpose of placing words, which is to convey and receive meanings. (His statement: upon the animal or the rational) i.e., its signification upon one of these two individually, not upon the combination; otherwise it would be correspondence, and therefore it is connected with 'or'. (His statement: and upon the external) he did not restrict it to the necessary, and he said after it: 'and necessity must be rational or customary... etc.' as a warning that necessity is a condition for the realization of implicative signification, not a differentia, so that the restriction of signification to three types is not invalidated by allowing its signification upon an external that is not necessary. Al-Jalal al-Dawwani added: 'And if it entered into its concept, the condition would be redundant,' as some glosses said.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage defines dalaalat al-iltizam (signification by implication). The definition states that it is signification of a word for something external to its placed meaning, but which necessarily accompanies it (luzum). Dasuqi emphasizes that necessity is a condition, not a differentia. Then Attar criticizes a previous claim about a certain issue (likely referring to an earlier discussion about tadammun). He argues that it is unreasonable because the lawgiver (wadi') is wise and would not place a word for a composite meaning where one part is unspecified. He also notes that this contradicts the purpose of language, which is to convey meanings. Then there is a comment explaining that 'on the animal or the rational' means each separately, not the combination, otherwise it would be mutabaqa. Finally, it clarifies that the term 'external' is not restricted to necessary implications, but necessity is required; otherwise, the restriction of signification to three types would not be rational. Al-Jalal al-Dawwani added that if the implication entered into the concept, the condition would be redundant.

Key Terms
دلالة الالتزام
لزوم
الوضع

Checkpoint

A) The external meaning must be part of the original meaning.
B) The external meaning must be logically or customarily necessary (luzum).
C) The external meaning must be explicitly mentioned in the definition.
D) The word must have multiple meanings.

Key Takeaway
Luzum is a necessary condition for dalaalat al-iltizam, distinguishing it from arbitrary external relations and preserving the tripartite division of signification.

?

The Three Types of Conventional Signification and the Condition of Necessary Concomitance
Defines three types of conventional signification and clarifies the role of necessary concomitance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of conventional signification and explain why necessary concomitance is a condition for implicative signification, not a part of its definition.

Core Idea
Implicative signification requires a necessary connection, but that connection is not in its definition.

In this passage, the commentator explains the three types of conventional signification: conforming, inclusive, and implicative. The key insight is that for implicative signification, the external meaning must be necessarily connected to the designated meaning, but this necessary concomitance is only a condition for its actual occurrence, not a component of the definition. This distinction resolves many misunderstandings about the division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Find the three Arabic terms (al-mutabaqa, al-tadammun, al-iltizam) and their brief definitions in the passage. Note that they are all types of conventional (wad'iyya) signification.
2
Understand the inclusive type
Inclusive signification (tadammun) only occurs when the designated meaning has parts (compound). The example 'human' signifies 'animal' or 'rational' individually. Conforming signification applies to both compound and simple meanings.
Contrast with conforming: conforming is more general.
3
Focus on implicative
Implicative signification (iltizam) is defined as signification upon a meaning external to the designated. The passage stresses that necessary concomitance (luzum) is a condition (shart) for its realization, not a differentia (fasl) in the definition.
If luzum were part of the definition, the condition would be redundant.
4
Apply the division to an Islamic example
Take the word 'salat' (prayer): its conforming signification is the entire set of actions; inclusive signification is each component like ruku' or sujud; implicative signification could be 'submission to Allah' as a necessary external meaning. Check which type fits each.
This shows how the tool is used in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَضَمُّنُ لكون الجزء في ضمن المعنى الموضوع له كـ: دلالة الإنسان على الحيوانِ أو النَّاطِقِ . دلالة الالتزام وَ دلالته عَلَى الْخَارج عن المعنى الموضوع له التزام ؛ له الدسوقي مركَّباً كـ حيوان ناطق، الذي وضع له إنسان، فدلالة التضمنِ إِنَّمَا تكونُ فيما لهُ جزء، وهو المعنى المركَّبُ ؛ بخلافِ الدَّلالةِ المطابقيَّة، فإنَّها تكون في ذلك وفيما لا جزء له ؛ كالنُّقطة والجوهر الفرد، فتكون المطابقيَّةُ أعمَّ مِنَ التَّضمنيَّة عموماً مطلقاً، وقولُهُ: تَضَمُّن؛ أي: تُسمَّى تَضمَّناً ؛ أي: دلالةً تضمن. قَوْلُهُ : لِكَوْنِ الْجُزْء... إلخ عِلَّةٌ لِتَسميتها تضمُّنيَّة، وقوله: كَدلالة الإنسان؛ أي : كدلالة لفظ الإنسان الموضوع للحيوانِ النَّاطِقِ في حال إطلاقه على ذلك. قَوْلُهُ : وَدَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى الْخَارج أي : على الخارج عن الموضوع له اللازم له ؛ لأنَّ اللُّزومَ شرطُ في تحقق الالتزاميَّة، وقوله: التزام؛ أي: تُسمى التزاماً ؛ أي: دلالة التزام. العطّار المطابقيّ ؛ فَتَدبَّرُ . ا.هـ . أقولُ : تَدَبَّرْنَاهُ فَوَجَدْنَاهُ غير معقولٍ، فَإِنَّ الدَّلالةَ مُتفرّعةُ على الوضع، وبعد العِلْم بأنَّ هذا اللَّفْظَ مَوضُوعٌ لِهَذا المعنى المركَّب، ومعلوم ارتباط أحد الجزأين بالآخَرِ ، كيفَ يُقَالُ مَا ذكر والواضِعُ حَكِيمٌ؟ فكيفَ يضعُ لفظاً لمعنِّى مُركَّب؛ جزؤُهُ الثَّاني غيرُ مُعيَّن يُوجُوبِ تَعيُّنِ الموضوع له حالة الوضع؟ وأيضاً هذا مُنَافٍ لغرض وضع الألفاظ، وهوَ إفادة المعاني واستفادتها . : قَوْلُهُ : على الْحَيَوَانِ أَوِ النَّاطِقِ أي دلالته على واحدٍ مِن هَذَين على انفرادِهِ؛ لا على المجموع، وإلا ؛ كانَ مُطَابقةً، ولِذلِكَ عطفَ بِأو . قَوْلُهُ : وَعَلَى الْخَارج لم يقيَّده باللازم، وقال بعدَهُ : ولا بُدَّ مِنَ اللُّزومِ عَقْلاً أو عرفاً ... إلخ؛ تنبيهاً على أنَّ اللُّزومَ شَوْطٌ لِتحققِ الدَّلالةِ الالتزاميَّة؛ لا فصل، فَلَا يبطلُ كَوْنُ حَصْرِ الدَّلالةِ في الثَّلاثِ عقليًّا بِتَجويز دلالته على خارج غيرِ لازم، زاد الجلالُ الدَّوَّانيُّ : ولو دخل في مفهومِهِ؛ لَغَا الاشتراط، قاله بعضُ الحواشي، فَصْلٌ: في تعريفِ الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ وأحكامها لكون الخارج لازماً للمعنى الموضوع له الدسوقي قَوْلُهُ : لِكَوْنِ الْخَارِج ... إلخ علَّةٌ لتسميتها دلالة التزاميَّة . العطار بیانه ۲۰۷ لفظ وتحرير المقامِ أنَّ الدَّوَانيُّ قال: حضرُ الدَّلالة الوضعيّة في الثلاثةِ عَقلِي، فَإِنَّ اللُّزوم شَرطُ تحقُّقِ الدَّلالةِ الالتزاميَّةِ وليسَ مُعتبراً في حدّها ا.هـ . وَوَجَّهَهُ أبو الفتح بأنَّ العقل يجزمُ بالحصرِ بِمُجرَّدِ مُلاحظةِ مَفهوم هذهِ القِسمَةِ، قال: وأورد عليهِ أَنَّهَ إِنَّما يكون عقليا إنْ لم تُقيَّد مفهوماتُها بِقَيْدِ الحيثيَّةِ كَمَا وقع في عبارة المتأخرين، واشتهر بين المحصلينَ، فَلَا يكونُ عقليًّا، بل استقرائيا لِجَوازِ أَنْ يدلَّ لفظ على جزء الموضوع لهُ لَا لِكَونِهِ جُزءاً منهُ بَلْ لِكَونِهِ لَازِمَاً لِجزء الموضوعِ لَه كما إذا وُضِعَ بإزاء مفهوم مُركَّبٍ مِنَ الملزومِ واللازم أو لِكَونِهِ جزءاً لجزء الموضوعِ لَهُ أو لكونه لازماً للازم الموضوع لَهُ أو لِكَونِهِ مُجزءاً للازم الموضوع له إلى غير ذلكَ مِنَ الاعتباراتِ الَّتي ذكرَهَا ، قال : وجوابُهُ أَنَّ قيد الحيثيَّةِ هَهُنا بمعنى التَّعليل المتعلِّقِ بنفس الوضع، وباقي القيود لتعيين ذلك الوضع المعلَّلِ بِهِ كَمَا هو المتبادرُ مِن عِبارةِ صَاحِبِ الكَشْفِ والكاتبي الكَشْفِ والكاتبي، لا بمعنى التَّعليل المتعلّق بالوضع مع باقي القيود، وحاصِلُ التَّعريفاتِ أنَّ المطابقة دلالة اللفظ على معنّى بواسطة الوضع الذي ذلك المعنى تمام الموضوع له بذلك الوضع ، والتَّضمُّنُ دلالةُ اللَّفْظِ على معنّى بواسطة الوضع الذي ذلك المعنى جزء الموضوع له بذلك، والالتزام دلالةُ اللَّفْظِ على معنِّى بواسطة الوضْعِ الَّذي ذلك المعنى خارج عَنِ الموضوعِ لَهُ بذلك الوضع، ولا يَخفَى أنَّهُ على هذا ؛ لا يُتصوَّرُ واسطةٌ بين الأقسامِ الثَّلاثةِ، والوسائط المذكورة مندرجة تحتَهَا قَطعاً ؛ ضَرورة أنَّ ما يتعلَّقُ بِنَفْسِ الموضوع لَهُ مُندَرج في مفهوم المطابقة، وَمَا يتعلَّقُ بجزئِهِ مُندرج في مفهومِ التَّضمُّنِ ، ومَا يتعلّقُ بِخَارِجِ الموضوعِ لَهُ مُندَرج في مفهوم الالتزام، ثمَّ قَالَ : فَظَهَرَ أَنَّ قولَهُ : فإِنَّ اللُّزومَ شَرْطُ تَحقُّقِ الدَّلالةِ الالتزاميَّةِ ... إلخ؛ كلام حقٌّ ليس فيه أثرُ لِلإهمال كَمَا توهَّمَهُ بعضُ الشَّارِحِينَ ا.هـ . وفي حاشية مير زاهد أنَّ المعتبر في حد دلالة الالتزام هو الخروج بدونِ اعتبارِ اللُّزومِ، وَهُوَ عبارةٌ عن عدم العينيَّةِ والجزئية، فيكونُ حَصْرُ الدَّلالةِ الوضعيَّةِ اللَّفظِيَّةِ في
Inclusive: because the part is within the meaning designated by the word, like the signification of 'human' upon 'animal' or 'rational'. Implicative signification: and its signification upon what is external to the designated meaning is implication. Dusuqi: compound, like 'rational animal', which is designated by 'human'. So inclusive signification only occurs in what has a part, which is the compound meaning; unlike conforming signification, for it occurs in that and in what has no part, like the point and the individual substance. Thus conforming is more general than inclusive in absolute generality. His statement: 'tadammun' means it is called tadammun, i.e., inclusive signification. His statement: 'because the part... etc.' is a reason for calling it inclusive. His statement: 'like the signification of human' means like the signification of the word 'human' which is designated for 'rational animal' when uttered for that. His statement: 'and its signification upon what is external' means upon what is external to the designated meaning and necessary for it, because necessary concomitance is a condition for the realization of implicative signification. His statement: 'implication' means it is called implication, i.e., implicative signification. Al-'Attar: the conforming; so reflect. End quote. I say: we reflected and found it unintelligible, for signification is dependent on convention, and after knowing that this word is designated for this compound meaning and that the connection of one part to the other is known, how can what is mentioned be said? And the positor is wise? So how can he posit a word for a compound meaning whose second part is unspecified, whereas the designated must be specified at the time of positing? Also this contradicts the purpose of positing words, which is to convey meanings and understand them. His statement: 'upon animal or rational' means its signification upon each of these individually, not upon the combination; otherwise it would be conforming, and therefore he used 'or'. His statement: 'and upon what is external' he did not restrict it to the necessary, and he said after it: 'there must be necessary concomitance, either rationally or conventionally... etc.' as a warning that necessary concomitance is a condition for the realization of implicative signification, not a differentia, so it does not invalidate the division of signification into three being rational, by allowing its signification upon an external that is not necessary. Al-Jalal al-Dawwani added: if it were part of its concept, the condition would be redundant, as some glossators stated. Section: On the definition of the three types of signification and their rulings. Because the external is necessary for the designated meaning. Dusuqi: His statement: 'because the external... etc.' is a reason for calling it implicative signification. Al-'Attar: His explanation: Word 207. And the clarification of the matter is that al-Dawwani said: The division of conventional signification into three is rational, for necessary concomitance is a condition for the realization of implicative signification and is not considered in its definition. End quote. Abu al-Fath justified it by saying that the mind judges the division merely by observing the concept of this division. He said: It was objected that it would be rational only if its concepts were not restricted by a qualification of 'with respect to' (haythiyya), as is found in the expression of the later scholars and is well-known among the accomplished; thus it would not be rational but inductive, because it is possible that a word signifies a part of the designated meaning not because it is a part of it but because it is necessary for a part of the designated meaning, as when it is posited for a compound concept consisting of the necessary and the necessitated, or because it is a part of a part of the designated, or because it is necessary for the necessary of the designated, or because it is a component of the necessary of the designated, and other such considerations that were mentioned. He said: The answer is that the qualification 'with respect to' here means the cause related to the positing itself, and the other qualifications are to specify that positing which is caused, as is evident from the expression of the author of al-Kashf and al-Katibi; not in the sense of the cause related to the positing together with the other qualifications. The summary of the definitions is that conforming is the signification of a word upon a meaning by means of the positing of which that meaning is the entire designated for that positing; inclusive is the signification of a word upon a meaning by means of the positing of which that meaning is a part of the designated for that; implicative is the signification of a word upon a meaning by means of the positing of which that meaning is external to the designated for that positing. It is not hidden that on this basis, no intermediate between the three divisions is conceivable, and the mentioned intermediates are certainly included under them, necessarily because what pertains to the designated itself is included in the concept of conforming, what pertains to its part is included in the concept of inclusive, and what pertains to what is external to the designated is included in the concept of implicative. Then he said: So it is evident that his statement: 'For necessary concomitance is a condition for the realization of implicative signification... etc.' is correct speech with no trace of negligence, as some commentators imagined. End quote. And in the gloss of Mir Zahid, that what is considered in the definition of implicative signification is externality without considering necessary concomitance, and it is an expression of not being identical and not being a part, so the division of conventional verbal signification into
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the three types of conventional signification (dalala wad'iyya): conforming (mutabaqa), inclusive (tadammun), and implicative (iltizam). The author begins by defining inclusive signification: it is the signification of a word upon a part of its designated meaning, giving the example of 'human' signifying 'animal' or 'rational' individually. He notes that inclusive signification only applies to compound meanings (those having parts), unlike conforming signification which applies to both simple and compound. The passage then defines implicative signification as signification upon an external meaning that is necessary for the designated meaning, emphasizing that necessary concomitance (luzum) is a condition for its realization, not a part of its definition. The commentator al-'Attar raises an objection: if a word is posited for a compound meaning whose second part is unspecified, that would be irrational and contradict the purpose of positing words. The reply clarifies that the word 'or' in the example indicates the parts individually, not the compound. The passage then cites al-Dusuqi and al-Dawwani arguing that the condition of luzum is not part of the definition, otherwise it would be redundant. The discussion continues with the objection that the division into three might not be a priori (aqli) but inductive (istiqrai) if the concepts are qualified by 'with respect to' (haythiyya), citing possibilities like a word signifying a part of the designated not as a part but as necessary for a part. The answer is that the qualification 'with respect to' here refers to the cause related to positing itself, not to the resulting signification, thus preserving the a priori nature of the division. Finally, the passage summarizes the three definitions: conforming: the word signifies the entire designated meaning; inclusive: the word signifies a part of the designated; implicative: the word signifies something external to the designated. All possible intermediaries are included under these three, and the condition of luzum is correctly understood as a condition for existence, not part of the definition. The gloss of Mir Zahid further states that the definition of implicative considers only externality (khuruj) without luzum, meaning that the word signifies something that is neither identical nor a part of the designated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is necessary concomitance (luzum) considered a condition and not part of the definition of implicative signification?
A) Because it would make the division into three types not a priori.
B) Because if it were part of the definition, the condition would be redundant.
C) Because the positor is wise and would not include it.
D) Because it would contradict the purpose of positing words.

Key Takeaway
The three types of conventional signification are distinguished by whether the meaning is the whole, a part, or external, and implicative requires necessary connection for actualization, not for definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which type of signification (mutabaqa, tadammun, or iltizam) is used in the following: The word 'yad' (hand) in the verse 'wa al-sariqu wa al-sariqatu faqta'u aydiyahuma' (the thief, male and female, amputate their hands). Does 'hand' signify by conforming, inclusive, or implicative the entire limb from the wrist? Explain your reasoning using the criteria from this lesson.
?
Take the term 'khamr' (wine). Its designated meaning is a specific intoxicating drink. Give an example of its signification by conforming, by inclusive, and by implicative, ensuring you respect the condition of necessary concomitance for the implicative case.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
10 min
The Three Types of Implication: Mutabaqa, Tadammun, Iltizam
The author defines mutabaqa, tadammun, and iltizam and debates the rational nature of their classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify any given conventional verbal implication as mutabaqa, tadammun, or iltizam, and explain why the classification is rationally exhaustive.

Core Idea
The three implications form a rational, exhaustive division of verbal conventional meaning.

In this section, the author defines the three types of conventional verbal implication: mutabaqa (conformity), tadammun (inclusion), and iltizam (implication). The passage not only provides clear definitions but also defends the claim that these three categories are rationally exhaustive, addressing objections about the role of 'haythiyya' (consideration). By understanding this classification, you will gain a fundamental tool for analyzing how words convey meaning in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three implications
Locate the definitions of mutabaqa, tadammun, and iltizam in the Arabic text. Note that mutabaqa is implication for the full assigned meaning, tadammun for a part, and iltizam for something external but necessarily connected.
The definitions are summarized after the discussion of haythiyya.
2
Understand the debate on rational vs. empirical classification
The passage presents an objection: if the definitions require a haythiyya condition, the classification becomes empirical rather than rational. Follow the reasoning: al-Dawani claims it is rational because the mind grasps the division merely by understanding the concepts. The objection says haythiyya restricts the concepts, making the division empirical. The answer is that haythiyya here does not restrict but rather clarifies the rationale behind the positing.
Pay attention to how the answer uses 'haythiyya' to prevent overlap, not to exclude any possible implication.
3
Analyze the refutation of intermediates
The passage asserts that no intermediate category exists: anything pertaining to the subject matter itself is mutabaqa, to a part is tadammun, and to an external is iltizam. Test this claim: consider whether some implications might be borderline. The text argues that all possibilities are covered.
This step reinforces the exhaustiveness of the threefold division.
4
See the example of iltizam: 'human' implying 'capacity for knowledge'
The author gives the example of 'human' implying the capacity for knowledge and writing. Recognize that this is iltizam because the capacity is external to the definition of human (rational animal) but necessarily connected. The commentary notes that a better example would be 'blindness' implying 'sight', as the necessity is more evident.
This example illustrates how iltizam works in practice.

لفظ
وتحرير المقامِ أنَّ الدَّوَانيُّ قال: حضرُ الدَّلالة الوضعيّة في الثلاثةِ عَقلِي، فَإِنَّ اللُّزوم شَرطُ تحقُّقِ الدَّلالةِ الالتزاميَّةِ وليسَ مُعتبراً في حدّها ا.هـ. ، وَوَجَّهَهُ أبو الفتح بأنَّ العقل يجزمُ بالحصرِ بِمُجرَّدِ مُلاحظةِ مَفهوم هذهِ القِسمَةِ، قال: وأورد عليهِ أَنَّهَ إِنَّما يكون عقليا إنْ لم تُقيَّد مفهوماتُها بِقَيْدِ الحيثيَّةِ كَمَا وقع في عبارة المتأخرين، واشتهر بين المحصلينَ، فَلَا يكونُ عقليًّا، بل استقرائيا لِجَوازِ أَنْ يدلَّ لفظ على جزء الموضوع لهُ لَا لِكَونِهِ جُزءاً منهُ بَلْ لِكَونِهِ لَازِمَاً لِجزء الموضوعِ لَه كما إذا وُضِعَ بإزاء مفهوم مُركَّبٍ مِنَ الملزومِ واللازم أو لِكَونِهِ جزءاً لجزء الموضوعِ لَهُ أو لكونه لازماً للازم الموضوع لَهُ أو لِكَونِهِ مُجزءاً للازم الموضوع له إلى غير ذلكَ مِنَ الاعتباراتِ الَّتي ذكرَهَا ، قال : وجوابُهُ أَنَّ قيد الحيثيَّةِ هَهُنا بمعنى التَّعليل المتعلِّقِ بنفس الوضع، وباقي القيود لتعيين ذلك الوضع المعلَّلِ بِهِ كَمَا هو المتبادرُ مِن عِبارةِ صَاحِبِ الكَشْفِ والكاتبي الكَشْفِ والكاتبي، لا بمعنى التَّعليل المتعلّق بالوضع مع باقي القيود، وحاصِلُ التَّعريفاتِ أنَّ المطابقة دلالة اللفظ على معنّى بواسطة الوضع الذي ذلك المعنى تمام الموضوع له بذلك الوضع ، والتَّضمُّنُ دلالةُ اللَّفْظِ على معنّى بواسطة الوضع الذي ذلك المعنى جزء الموضوع له بذلك، والالتزام دلالةُ اللَّفْظِ على معنِّى بواسطة الوضْعِ الَّذي ذلك المعنى خارج عَنِ الموضوعِ لَهُ بذلك الوضع، ولا يَخفَى أنَّهُ على هذا ؛ لا يُتصوَّرُ واسطةٌ بين الأقسامِ الثَّلاثةِ، والوسائط المذكورة مندرجة تحتَهَا قَطعاً ؛ ضَرورة أنَّ ما يتعلَّقُ بِنَفْسِ الموضوع لَهُ مُندَرج في مفهوم المطابقة، وَمَا يتعلَّقُ بجزئِهِ مُندرج في مفهومِ التَّضمُّنِ ، ومَا يتعلّقُ بِخَارِجِ الموضوعِ لَهُ مُندَرج في مفهوم الالتزام، ثمَّ قَالَ : فَظَهَرَ أَنَّ قولَهُ : فإِنَّ اللُّزومَ شَرْطُ تَحقُّقِ الدَّلالةِ الالتزاميَّةِ ... إلخ؛ كلام حقٌّ ليس فيه أثرُ لِلإهمال كَمَا توهَّمَهُ بعضُ الشَّارِحِينَ ا.هـ. وفي حاشية مير زاهد أنَّ المعتبر في حد دلالة الالتزام هو الخروج بدونِ اعتبارِ اللُّزومِ، وَهُوَ عبارةٌ عن عدم العينيَّةِ والجزئية، فيكونُ حَصْرُ الدَّلالةِ الوضعيَّةِ اللَّفظِيَّةِ في
الثَّلاثِ عقليًا، فإنَّ الحصر العقلي هو أنْ يكونَ دائِراً بينَ النَّفي والإثباتِ؛ سواءٌ كَانَ عنوان النَّفْيِ مَذْكُوراً فيه أو لا، فإنْ قُلْتَ: لا بُدَّ في حدودِ الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ مِن اعتبارِ الحيثياتِ على مَا ذَكَرُوا في جوابِ النَّقْضِ المشهور، وحينئذ لا يكونُ الحَصْرُ عقليا ، قُلْتُ : المعتبر في حد الالتزام حيثيَّةُ العينيَّة والجزئية؛ لَا حيثيَّةُ عدم العينيَّةِ والجزئيَّةِ، وَهُوَ كافٍ في جوابِ النَّقْضِ المشهور .ا.هـ. وقَولُهُ: سواءٌ كَانَ عنوان النَّفي مذكوراً فيه أو لا ؛ يعني : أنَّه لا يُشترط تردُّدُهُ بالنَّفْيِ والإثباتِ وإِنْ كانَ الأكثر فيهِ ذَلكَ فإنْ أُريد ترديد الحصْرِ هُنا بينَ النَّفْي والإثباتِ؛ قِيلَ في توجيهِ الحَصْرِ اللَّفْظِ إمَّا على نَفْسِ الموضوع له وهي المطابقة أو لا، وحينئذٍ إِمَّا أن يكون على
مُجُزئِهِ وهي التَّضمُّنُ أو لا، وهي الالتزام، فإنَّ العقل يجزم بالانحصار بمجرَّدِ مُلاحظةِ القِسمَةِ كما قُلْنَا، وأجابَ عبد الحكيم أيضاً بأنَّ قيد الحيثيَّةِ إِنَّمَا اعتُبِرَ لِئَلَّا يلزم تداخل الأقسامِ ، لا لإخراجِ فَرْدٍ مِنَ الدَّلالةِ اللَّفظيَّةِ الوضعيَّةِ مِنَ الأقسامِ الثَّلاثةِ، ثم قال بعدَ أَنْ أوردَ على الحَصْرِ أُموراً : إِنَّ وُرودَ هَذِهِ الشُّكوكِ على الحَصْرِ المذكورِ لا يُنافي كَونَهُ عقليا ؛ لأنَّ البديهي قَدْ تتطرقُ إليهِ الشُّبهةُ بواسطة عدمِ تحريرِ الطَّرفَيْن كما هو مناطُ الحُكْمِ .ا.هـ.
(قَوْلُهُ : كَدَلَالَةِ الْإِنْسَانِ عَلَى قَابِل الْعِلْمِ وَصَنْعَةِ الْكِتَابَةِ) لو مَثَّلَ بلزومِ البَصَرِ للعمى ؛ لَكَانَ جارياً على ما هو المختارُ مِنْ أنَّ المعتبر هو اللزومُ البَيِّنُ بالمعنى الأخص واستغنى عن البحث الآتي، وجَوَابُهُ، وَلَعَلَّهُ إنَّما مَثَلَ ذكرهُ تبعاً لِما وقع مِن بعضهم لينبه على ما فيهِ مِنَ البحث والجواب ؛ تنبيهاً للطلاب كما يشيرُ لِذلك قوله :
وهذا البحث وإنْ كانَ ... إلخ.
Section: On Defining the Three Implications and Their Rulings
Because the external is necessary for the meaning assigned to.
Al-Dusuqi: His statement: 'Because the external... etc.' is a cause for naming it 'implicative implication'.
Al-Attar: His explanation.
And the clarification of the position is that al-Dawani said: The specification of conventional implication in the three is rational, for the necessity is a condition for the realization of implicative implication but is not considered in its definition. (End). And Abu al-Fath explained it by saying: The mind judges the confinement merely by observing the meaning of this division. He said: And it was objected to him that it would be rational only if their concepts were not restricted by a condition of 'haythiyya' (respect), as occurred in the expression of the later scholars and became well-known among the investigators. So it is not rational but rather inductive (empirical), because it is possible that a word indicates a part of the subject matter not because it is a part of it but because it is necessary for a part of the subject matter, as when it is placed for a compound concept consisting of the necessary and the necessary, or because it is a part of a part of the subject matter, or because it is necessary for the necessary of the subject matter, or because it is a part of the necessary for the subject matter, and so on among the considerations that he mentioned. He said: And the answer to it is that the condition of 'haythiyya' here is in the sense of the rationale pertaining to the act of positing itself, and the remaining conditions are for specifying that positing which is given a rationale, as is the apparent from the expression of the author of al-Kashf and al-Katibi, not in the sense of the rationale pertaining to the positing together with the remaining conditions. And the summary of the definitions is: Mutabaqa is the implication of a word for a meaning by means of the positing according to which that meaning is the full subject matter of that positing; Tadammun is the implication of a word for a meaning by means of the positing according to which that meaning is part of the subject matter of that positing; and Iltizam is the implication of a word for a meaning by means of the positing according to which that meaning is external to the subject matter of that positing. And it is not hidden that on this basis, no intermediate between the three categories is conceivable, and the mentioned intermediates are definitely subsumed under them, necessarily, because what pertains to the subject matter itself falls under the concept of mutabaqa, what pertains to its part falls under the concept of tadammun, and what pertains to outside the subject matter falls under the concept of iltizam. Then he said: So it became clear that his saying: 'For the necessity is a condition for the realization of implicative implication... etc.' is correct speech, with no trace of negligence as some of the commentators imagined. (End). And in the gloss of Mir Zahid: The considered factor in the definition of implicative implication is externality without consideration of necessity, and it is an expression of non-identity and non-partiality. So the confinement of conventional verbal implication to three is rational, for rational confinement is that which revolves between negation and affirmation, whether the term of negation is mentioned in it or not. For if you say: In the definitions of the three implications there must be consideration of the respects (al-haythiyyat) as they mentioned in answering the famous objection, and then the confinement would not be rational. I say: The considered factor in the definition of iltizam is the respect of identity and partiality; not the respect of non-identity and non-partiality, and that suffices in answering the famous objection. (End). And his saying: 'whether the term of negation is mentioned in it or not' means that it is not required that it be alternated between negation and affirmation, even though most often that is the case. For if one intends to alternate the confinement here between negation and affirmation, it is said in explaining the confinement: The word is either upon the subject matter itself—that is mutabaqa—or not, and then either upon its part—that is tadammun—or not—that is iltizam. For the mind judges the confinement merely by observing the division as we said. And Abd al-Hakim also answered that the condition of 'haythiyya' is only considered to prevent overlap of categories, not to exclude any individual of conventional verbal implication from the three categories. Then he said after enumerating some doubts about the confinement: The occurrence of these doubts about the mentioned confinement does not contradict its being rational, because the axiomatic may be subject to doubt due to lack of refinement of the two sides, as that is the basis of judgment. (End).
(His statement: Like the implication of 'human' for the capacity for knowledge and the craft of writing) If he had given an example of the necessity of sight for blindness, it would have been in accordance with what is chosen—that the considered factor is the evident necessity in the most specific sense—and he would have dispensed with the subsequent discussion and its answer. Perhaps he only gave this example following what occurred from some to alert them to what is in it of discussion and answer, as an alert to students, as his statement indicates: 'And this discussion, even if... etc.'
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definitions of the three types of implication (dalalat): mutabaqa (conformity), tadammun (inclusion), and iltizam (implication). It begins by stating that the section is on defining these three implications and their rulings. The commentator (likely Dusuqi) explains that the term 'external' in the definition of iltizam refers to something that is necessary for the assigned meaning, which is why it is called 'implicative implication'. The core of the passage is a debate about whether the classification of verbal conventional implication into exactly these three types is rational (aqli) or empirical (istiqrai). Al-Dawani asserted that the classification is rational because the mind can grasp the confinement merely by understanding the concepts. However, an objection is raised: if the definitions are restricted by a condition of 'haythiyya' (respect or consideration), then the classification is not rational but empirical, because different respects could produce intermediates. The answer given is that the haythiyya here is not a condition for exclusion but rather a way to avoid overlap; the definitions themselves, without the haythiyya, still yield a rational confinement. The passage then provides clear definitions: mutabaqa is when the word indicates the full meaning intended by the positing; tadammun is when it indicates a part of that meaning; iltizam is when it indicates something external to that meaning. It emphasizes that no intermediate exists because anything related to the meaning itself is mutabaqa, anything related to a part is tadammun, and anything external is iltizam. The commentary also discusses Mir Zahid's view that the definition of iltizam focuses on 'externality' without considering necessity, making the confinement rational. The famous objection about the need for haythiyyat is answered by stating that the considered respect in iltizam is that of 'identity and partiality', not their absence. Finally, the passage gives an example: the word 'human' indicates the capacity for knowledge and writing, which are external to the meaning of 'rational animal' but necessary for it. The commentator notes that a better example would have been the implication of 'blindness' for 'sight', as the necessity there is more evident, but the given example serves to alert students to potential discussions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of iltizam?
A) The word 'human' implying 'animal' because 'animal' is part of the definition.
B) The word 'human' implying 'rational' because 'rational' is part of the definition.
C) The word 'human' implying 'capacity for writing' because it is a necessary consequence, though not part of the definition.
D) The word 'human' implying 'alive' because 'alive' is a broader category.

Key Takeaway
The three implications—mutabaqa, tadammun, iltizam—form a rationally exhaustive classification of conventional verbal meaning, with no intermediates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the word 'zakat' implying 'purity' or 'blessing' is mutabaqa, tadammun, or iltizam. Explain your reasoning based on the definitions in the passage.
?
Take the term 'iman' (faith) as used in kalam. Its mutabaqa is 'belief in the heart with the tongue'. Tadammun would be 'belief in the heart' alone. Iltizam would be 'actions of the limbs'. Is this classification exhaustive? Defend your answer using the text's argument about no intermediates.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
5 min
The Rational Enumeration of the Three Denotations
Author argues that the division of denotations into three is rational, even considering the condition of aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a classification of verbal denotations is a rational enumeration by checking its exhaustiveness between affirmation and negation.

Core Idea
The three denotations are rationally exhaustive because they divide all possibilities: whole, part, or external.

In this passage, the commentator defends that the division of verbal denotation into conformity, inclusion, and implication is a rational enumeration (ḥaṣr 'aqlī) — not merely conventional. The objection that aspects (ḥaythiyyāt) are needed to define each type is addressed: these aspects only prevent overlap, not break exhaustiveness. You will learn what makes an enumeration rational and how to recognize one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The passage states that the three denotations are a rational enumeration. What definition does it give for rational enumeration? It says it 'revolves between negation and affirmation' — meaning it exhausts all possibilities whether negation is mentioned or not.
2
Understand the objection
Some argue that because we need to specify aspects (e.g., implication requires that the implied meaning is neither identical nor a part), the enumeration becomes conventional. Why would that be a problem? If it's based on arbitrary conventions, it wouldn't be rationally necessary.
3
Analyze the response
The commentator says that only positive aspects are considered (identity and partiality for implication), not their negations. How does this preserve rationality? The enumeration still relies on logical relations, not arbitrary choices.
4
Check the logical structure
The division is based on whether the denotation is for the whole (conformity), a part (inclusion), or something else (implication). Is this exhaustive? Does it leave any possibility? The intellect affirms that any denotation must fall into one of these three.
5
Apply to the doubt
Even if doubts arise, the passage argues that self-evident truths can be obscured by imprecise formulation. How does that relate to the rational nature of the enumeration? The doubts are due to lack of precision, not because the enumeration itself is flawed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي وضعَ العطار الثَّلاثِ عقليًا، فإنَّ الحصر العقلي هو أنْ يكونَ دائِراً بينَ النَّفي والإثباتِ؛ سواءٌ كَانَ عنوان النَّفْيِ مَذْكُوراً فيه أو لا، فإنْ قُلْتَ: لا بُدَّ في حدودِ الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ مِن اعتبارِ الحيثياتِ على مَا ذَكَرُوا في جوابِ النَّقْضِ المشهور، وحينئذ لا يكونُ الحَصْرُ عقليا ، قُلْتُ : المعتبر في حد الالتزام حيثيَّةُ العينيَّة والجزئية؛ لَا حيثيَّةُ عدم العينيَّةِ والجزئيَّةِ، وَهُوَ كافٍ في جوابِ النَّقْضِ المشهور .ا.هـ. وقَولُهُ: سواءٌ كَانَ عنوان النَّفي مذكوراً فيه أو لا ؛ يعني : أنَّه لا يُشترط تردُّدُهُ بالنَّفْيِ والإثباتِ وإِنْ كانَ الأكثر فيهِ ذَلكَ فإنْ أُريد ترديد الحصْرِ هُنا بينَ النَّفْي والإثباتِ؛ قِيلَ في توجيهِ الحَصْرِ اللَّفْظِ إِمَّا على نَفْسِ الموضوع له وهي المطابقة أو لا، وحينئذٍ إِمَّا أن يكون على دلالة مُجُزئِهِ وهي التَّضمُّنُ أو لا، وهي الالتزام، فإنَّ العقل يجزم بالانحصار بمجرَّدِ مُلاحظةِ القِسمَةِ كما قُلْنَا، وأجابَ عبد الحكيم أيضاً بأنَّ قيد الحيثيَّةِ إِنَّمَا اعتُبِرَ لِئَلَّا يلزم تداخل الأقسامِ ، لا لإخراجِ فَرْدٍ مِنَ الدَّلالةِ اللَّفظيَّةِ الوضعيَّةِ مِنَ الأقسامِ الثَّلاثةِ، ثم قال بعدَ أَنْ أوردَ على الحَصْرِ أُموراً : إِنَّ وُرودَ هَذِهِ الشُّكوكِ على الحَصْرِ المذكورِ لا يُنافي كَونَهُ عقليا ؛ لأنَّ البديهي قَدْ تتطرقُ إليهِ الشُّبهةُ بواسطة عدمِ تحريرِ الطَّرفَيْن كما هو مناطُ الحُكْمِ .ا.هـ.
(This is) what al-'Attar placed: the three (denotations) are rational. Indeed, the rational enumeration is that it revolves between negation and affirmation, whether the title of negation is mentioned in it or not. If you say: It is necessary in the limits of the three denotations to consider the aspects (al-haythiyyat) according to what they mentioned in the answer to the famous refutation, and in that case the enumeration would not be rational. I say: What is considered in the definition of implication is the aspect of identity and partiality, not the aspect of non-identity and non-partiality, and that is sufficient for the answer to the famous refutation. End. And his saying: 'whether the title of negation is mentioned in it or not' means that its alternation by negation and affirmation is not a condition, even if that is most common. If one intends to make the enumeration here alternate between negation and affirmation, it is said in directing the verbal enumeration: either it is for the thing itself — which is conformity — or not; and then either it is for the denotation of its part — which is inclusion — or not; and that is implication. For the intellect is certain of the exhaustiveness merely by observing the division as we said. And 'Abd al-Hakim also answered that the condition of aspect was only considered to prevent the overlap of the categories, not to exclude any individual from the three categories of conventional verbal denotation. Then he said after he raised some issues against the enumeration: Indeed, the occurrence of these doubts against the mentioned enumeration does not negate its being rational, because the self-evident may be subject to doubt due to the lack of precision of the two ends, which is the basis of judgment. End.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage defends the claim that the division of verbal denotation into three types (conformity, inclusion, and implication) is a rational enumeration (ḥaṣr 'aqlī). The commentator begins by stating that al-'Attar considered the three denotations to be rationally divided. A rational enumeration is defined as one that revolves between affirmation and negation — meaning it exhausts all possibilities, whether the negation is explicitly mentioned or not. A potential objection is raised: in defining each type, one must consider specific aspects (ḥaythiyyāt) to avoid overlap, such as the condition in implication that the implied meaning is neither identical nor a part of the literal meaning. This seems to make the enumeration conventional rather than rational. The response clarifies that in the definition of implication, only the positive aspects (identity and partiality) are considered — not their negations — and this suffices to answer the famous refutation. The commentator then explains that the condition of aspect is only to prevent the categories from overlapping, not to exclude any instance from the categories of conventional verbal denotation. Thus the enumeration remains rational because the intellect grasps the exhaustive division by simply observing the logical possibilities: either the denotation is for the whole (conformity), or for a part (inclusion), or for something external (implication). Even famous scholars like 'Abd al-Hakim confirm that the doubts raised do not negate the rational nature, as self-evident truths can be obscured by imprecise formulation, but the underlying rationality remains intact.

حيثية

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes the enumeration of the three denotations rational?
A) It is based on the authority of al-'Attar.
B) It revolves between affirmation and negation, covering all possibilities.
C) It requires specifying aspects to prevent overlap.
D) It is self-evident and cannot be doubted.

Key Takeaway
The division of verbal denotation into conformity, inclusion, and implication is a rational enumeration because it exhaustively covers all logical possibilities, verified by the intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take any Islamic legal text, such as the verse 'Establish prayer' (al-Baqara 2:43). Identify the three denotations of this command: conformity (the obligation to pray), inclusion (the obligation to perform specific acts within prayer like bowing), and implication (the obligation to avoid what invalidates prayer). Explain how these three exhaust the possible meanings.
?
Consider the definition of implication: it must be neither identical nor a part of the literal meaning. Why is it necessary to specify these aspects? Does specifying them make the enumeration non-rational? Defend your answer using the passage's argument.
