(قَوْلُهُ : بِأَلَّا يَكُوْنَ ... إِلَخ) الباء سبيَّةٌ أو للتَّصوير؛ أي: وصحة السكوتِ عليه مُصوَّرةٌ بأن لا يكونَ ذلكَ اللَّفْظُ المركَّبُ مُستدعياً ... إلخ . (قَوْلُهُ : مُسْتَدْعِيَاً) أي : مُقتضياً . (قَوْلُهُ : كَاسْتِدْعَاءِ ... إلخ) مثال للمنفي؛ أي: استدعاء كاستدعاء ... إلخ، لَا كاستدعاء الفضلاتِ كما في : ضرب زيد أمس، فلو حذفتَ أمس ؛ لَكانَ الكلام تاما. العطار: اعتراضُ بعض الحواشِي بأنَّ تعريف المعنى لَا إشعارَ لَهُ بِكَونِهِ مَقصوداً ؛ فممنوع لأنَّ القَصْدَ نسبةٌ؛ أحد طرفيها المعنى، والطَّرَفُ الآخَرُ اللَّفْظُ، إذ يوصَفُ اللّفظ بكونه مقصوداً منه المعنى عند تعلَّقِ القصدِ المبني للفاعل بِهِ، فَلَا جَرَمَ يكون ذلكَ بِكَونِهِ الوصفُ حاصلاً للمعنى عندَ القَصْدِ والتَّعريفُ مُشِيرٌ إِلى هَذا الوَصْفِ؛ تَأَمَّلْ. (قَوْلُهُ : إِمَّا تَامٌ) الأَوْلَى : إِمَّا مُركَّبُ تَامّ؛ لأنَّهُ الاسم، لكنَّهُم كثيراً ما يتسامحونَ في أمثال ذلك . (قَوْلُهُ : كَاسْتِدْعَاءِ) صفةٌ مصدرٍ محذوفٍ؛ أي : مُستدعياً استدعاء كاستدعاء، وأشار بذلك إلى أنَّ الإسناد يتمُّ بالمسندِ إليه والمسندِ، ولا يُنافي ذلكَ توقُفُ الفعل المتعدي على مفعوله أو قيدهِ كالحالِ مثلاً، فإنَّ ذلكَ مِمَّا تكثرُ بِهِ الفائدة وتتربّى ولا يتوقَّفُ حصولها عليه، فانتِظَارُ المفعول بهِ أو الحالِ ليس كانتظار المسندِ إليه أو المسنَدِ، ونقل المحشّي هنا عن السَّيِّدِ الصَّفوي كلاماً ادَّعَى البعضُ عدم صحتِهِ، وهو كَمَا قالَ، وَلولا خَوفُ الإطالة؛ لأشبعْنَا فيه المقالة.
Chapter on investigations of expressions. [Divisions of the composite] (A) Either complete, if silence upon it is valid, meaning that it does not require another word, like the requirement of the predicate for the subject, and vice versa. Al-Dasuqi: The complete: His saying 'if valid' means silence is deemed good. By validity is meant linguistic validity, which is being deemed good, not legal validity which is opposite to corruption, because an utterance is not described as valid or invalid. His saying 'that it not be' etc.: The ba' is for exemplification or depiction; i.e., the validity of silence upon it is depicted by that composite utterance not being in need of another word... His saying 'requiring' means necessitating. His saying 'like the requirement etc.' is an example of the negated; i.e., a requirement like the requirement..., not like the requirement of superfluous parts, as in 'Zayd struck yesterday', for if you delete 'yesterday', the speech would be complete. Al-'Attar: An objection by some marginal commentators that the definition of meaning does not indicate it being intended is rejected, because intention is a relation; one of its two sides is the meaning, and the other side is the utterance, since the utterance is described as meaning being intended from it when the active intention attaches to it. Hence that description necessarily occurs for the meaning upon intention, and the definition points to this description; reflect. His saying 'Either complete' — it would be better to say 'either a complete composite' because that is the name, but they often tolerate such things. His saying 'like the requirement' is an attribute of a deleted infinitive; i.e., requiring a requirement like the requirement, and he indicated by that that predication is completed by the subject and predicate, and that does not contradict the transitive verb's dependence on its object or its restriction like a state, for that increases benefit and multiplication, and its attainment does not depend on it. So waiting for the object or state is not like waiting for the subject or predicate. The commentator here reported from al-Sayyid al-Safawi a statement which some claimed is false, and it is as he said, and were it not for fear of prolongation, we would have elaborated fully on it.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a definitional section from the commentary on Tahzeeb al-Mantiq, specifically on the division of composite expressions. It opens with the chapter on investigations of expressions. The main text states that a composite is either 'tamm' (complete), defined as that upon which silence is valid, meaning it does not require another word to complete its meaning. The commentator, al-Dasuqi, explains that 'valid' here is linguistic, meaning it is considered good to stop on it, not legal validity. The condition 'that it not be requiring another word' is clarified: the composite must not stand in need of a further word in the way that a predicate requires a subject or vice versa. Al-Dasuqi gives an example: 'Zayd struck yesterday' if you delete 'yesterday', the speech is complete (tamm), but if you say 'Zayd struck' alone, it is not complete because it requires an object. Al-'Attar then addresses an objection that the definition of 'meaning' does not indicate intentionality, but he refutes it by explaining that intention is a relation between utterance and meaning. He also notes that the term 'tamm' is technically an adjective, but it is commonly used as a noun. The commentary further clarifies that predication (isnad) is completed by subject and predicate alone; transitive verbs' need for objects or states is of a different order, as it increases benefit but is not essential for completeness. The passage ends with a reference to a reported statement from al-Sayyid al-Safawi, which some claim false, but the commentator affirms its correctness without elaboration.

Key Terms
تام
مستدعي
صحة السكوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) ضرب زيد (Zaid struck)
C) ما زيد (What Zaid)
D) ضرب زيد أمس مع باقي جملة (Zaid struck yesterday with the rest of the sentence)

Key Takeaway
A complete composite (tamm) is defined by the validity of silence upon it, meaning it does not require another word for its essential predication; transitive verbs' needs for objects are not essential for completeness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Division of Compound Expressions: Tamm, Naqis, and Taqyidi
Author defines compound expressions as complete or incomplete, with restrictive as a subtype.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between complete (tamm) and incomplete (naqis) compound expressions, and identify the restrictive (taqyidi) subtype with examples from Arabic grammar.

Core Idea
Compound expressions are either complete sentences or incomplete constructions; incomplete ones that qualify a term are called restrictive.

This passage from a classical logic commentary lays out the fundamental division of compound expressions. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for analyzing linguistic arguments in Islamic sciences, where the precise form of an expression determines whether it can be evaluated as true or false.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish tamm and naqis
Determine whether the compound forms a complete sentence that can stand alone (tamm) or requires more completion (naqis).
Tamm includes both khabar and insha.
2
Identify the restrictive subtype
In a naqis compound, check if the second part qualifies the first (e.g., adjective, idafa, or circumstantial phrase).
The passage specifically defines restrictive as when the second qualifies the first.
3
Examine the commentary's terminological refinement
Note that the commentator suggests saying 'murakkab naqis' instead of just 'naqis' to avoid ambiguity.
This shows careful attention to precision in logical terminology.

فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظِ
- (أَوْ إِنْشَاءُ) إن لم يحتمل ذلك.
ب - (وَإِمَّا نَاقِصٌ) عطفٌ على قوله : «إمَّا تامٌ» .
• والمركَّبُ النَّاقصُ ؛ أي : الذي لا يصح الشكوتُ عليه :
- إِمَّا تَفْسِيدِيُّ) إن كانَ الثَّاني قيداً للأوَّل،
(قَوْلُهُ : أَوْ إِنْشَاءُ) وهو ما قارن معناه لفظَهُ؛ كَبِعْت، وأنتَ حرّ، واضرب. (قَوْلُهُ : إِنْ لَمْ يَحْتَمِلُ ذَلِكَ) أي : باعتبار مدلولِهِ المطابقي، وأمَّا بالنَّظرِ لِمدلوله الالتزامي ؛ فيحتملُ ذلك ؛ لأنَّ اضرب يستلزم أنا طالبٌ لِلضَّرب ، وذلك قولٌ مُحتمل . (قَوْلُهُ : وَإِمَّا نَاقِصُ الأَوْلَى : وإِمَّا مُركّب ناقص؛ لأنَّه الاسم لا مُجرَّد النقصان، وكذا يُقالُ في قوله: (تام). (قَوْلُهُ : إِنْ كَانَ الثَّانِي قَيْدَاً لِلْأَوَّلِ وصفاً كانَ أو مضافاً إليه أو غيرهما ؛ كَقَوْلِكَ : ضربَ في الدَّار ، من قولك : ضرب في الدَّارِ زيد.
العطار: (قَوْلُهُ : أَوْ إِنْشَاءُ) لا يتوهَّمُ أَنَّ التَّقابُلَ بينَ الخبر والإنشاء تقابل العدم والمَلَكَةِ؛ العدم معنًى واحدٌ ، والإنشاء حقائقُ مُختلفةٌ ؛ كالأمرِ والنَّهي وغيرِهما ؛ ضرورةً اختلافِ لوازمِهِمَا المستلزمة اختلاف الملزوماتِ ، بَل الظَّاهِرُ أنَّ بين الخبر والإنشاء تضادا حقيقيا، وبين أقسامهما تضاداً مشهوريًّا.
Chapter: On the investigation of expressions. - (Or a performative utterance) if it does not admit that. b - (Or incomplete) as a conjunction to his statement: 'Either complete.' • The incomplete compound; i.e., that upon which it is not valid to remain silent: - Either restrictive) if the second is a qualifier for the first. (His statement: 'Or a performative utterance') and it is that whose meaning accompanies its utterance; like 'I sold', 'you are free', and 'strike!'. (His statement: 'If it does not admit that') i.e., with respect to its literal signification; but with respect to its implicative signification, it admits that; because 'strike!' entails that I am a seeker of striking, and that is a statement that admits truth/falsity. (His statement: 'Or incomplete', preferable: 'Or an incomplete compound'; because it is a name, not mere incompleteness, and likewise is said in his statement: 'complete'). (His statement: 'If the second is a qualifier for the first', whether it is a description, or a genitive construction, or others; like your saying: 'struck in the house', from your saying: 'struck in the house Zayd'. al-Attar: (His statement: 'Or a performative utterance') one should not imagine that the opposition between informative and performative is an opposition of privation and possession; privation is a single meaning, while performatives are different realities; like command, prohibition, and others; due to the necessary difference of their concomitants which necessitates difference of the concomitants' objects; rather the apparent is that between informative and performative there is a real contrariety, and between their divisions there is a well-known contrariety.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory section from a commentary (sharh) on a logic text. It begins by stating the chapter topic: the investigation of expressions. The main text (matn) divides compound expressions: either they are complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis). The incomplete is further subdivided into restrictive (taqyidi) and non-restrictive. The author first clarifies the nature of 'insha' (performative utterance) in contrast to khabar (informative statement). Insha is defined as an utterance whose meaning coincides with its utterance; examples include 'I sold' (a sale contract), 'you are free' (manumission), and 'strike!' (command). Such utterances, in their literal signification, do not admit truth or falsity because they are not statements about something; however, in their implicative signification, they may imply a statement that is truth-apt (e.g., 'strike!' implies 'I am commanding striking', which is a statement). Then the author turns to the term 'naqis' (incomplete compound). A commentator suggests that the proper term is 'compound incomplete' (murakkab naqis) rather than just 'incomplete', because the latter is an abstract noun, whereas the intended meaning is a type of compound. The condition for a compound to be restrictive (taqyidi) is that the second word qualifies the first, whether as an adjective, a genitive construction, or other. An example given is 'daraba fi al-dar' (struck in the house) from the fuller expression 'daraba fi al-dar Zayd' (Zayd struck in the house). Here, 'fi al-dar' is a qualifier for the act of striking, making it restrictive. Finally, al-Attar adds a crucial conceptual clarification: the opposition between khabar and insha is not that of privation and possession (where one is the mere absence of the other), because insha encompasses diverse realities (command, prohibition, etc.), each with its own distinct concomitants. Rather, the opposition is a real contrariety (taddad haqiqi) between the two categories, and between their subdivisions there is a well-known contrariety. This guards against the misconception that insha is merely a deprivation of truth-value.

Key Terms
المركب التام
المركب الناقص
التركيب التقييدي
الخبر
الإنشاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a restrictive (taqyidi) compound?
A) 'Zayd stood' (Zayd qāma)
B) 'The book of Zayd' (kitāb Zayd)
C) 'Strike!' (iḍrib)
D) 'Zayd is standing' (Zayd qāʾim)

Key Takeaway
Compound expressions are classified based on whether they form complete sentences; within incomplete compounds, the restrictive type involves qualification of the first element by the second.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a restrictive compound from the following Arabic phrases: 'rajulun karimun' (generous man), 'qama Zaydun' (Zayd stood), 'bayt al-‘ilm' (house of knowledge).
?
Explain why 'khabar' is considered a complete compound (tamm) while 'insha' is also tamm but differs in truth-aptness.

The Logical Status of Insha: Performative Utterances
Author explains the truth-aptness of insha and its opposition to khabar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why insha (performative utterances) are not truth-apt in their primary signification, and why the opposition between khabar and insha is real contrariety, not privation.

Core Idea
Insha utterances like commands are not true or false, but their implicative meaning can be evaluated.

This lesson focuses on the nature of performative utterances (insha) as discussed in the commentary. The author distinguishes between literal and implicative signification, and al-Attar clarifies that khabar and insha are truly contrary categories, not merely one being the absence of the other.

Guided Path
1
Define khabar and insha
Distinguish between informative statements (khabar) that can be true/false, and performative utterances (insha) that accomplish an act by being uttered.
Examples: 'Zayd is standing' vs. 'Strike!'.
2
Analyze literal vs. implicative signification
In its literal meaning, insha like 'Strike!' cannot be true or false. But it implies a statement ('I command you to strike') that is truth-apt.
The passage uses the example of 'iḍrib'.
3
Examine al-Attar's contrariety argument
Al-Attar argues that the opposition between khabar and insha is not mere privation (absence of truth-value) but real contrariety, because insha encompasses diverse types with distinct properties.
This prevents reducing insha to a mere negative category.
4
Apply the distinction to Islamic legal utterances
In fiqh, utterances like 'I marry you' (zawwajtu) are insha; recognizing their inherent nature is crucial for understanding when they take effect.
Misclassifying them as khabar would lead to wrong conclusions about their validity conditions.

Understanding Taqyidi Compound: Restriction in Expression
Commentary analyzing compound expressions with example 'rāmi al-ḥijāra' and classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a taqyidi compound and distinguish it from non-taqyidi compounds, using examples from Arabic grammatical analysis.

Core Idea
A taqyidi compound is defined by its second part restricting the first.

In the study of compound expressions, logicians and grammarians distinguish between those where one part restricts the other (taqyidi) and those where it does not. This distinction is crucial for understanding how definitions and descriptions work in Islamic sciences. In this lesson, we will analyze the classic example 'rāmi al-ḥijāra' and explore the breadth of taqyidi compounds beyond just genitive and descriptive constructions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components of the compound
Take the example 'rāmi al-ḥijāra'. The first part is 'rāmi' (thrower) and the second is 'al-ḥijāra' (stones). Each contributes a part of the overall meaning.
2
Understand the function of the second part (qayd)
The second part 'al-ḥijāra' restricts the first, removing its absolute generality. Without it, 'rāmi' alone refers to any thrower; with it, it specifies the object thrown.
3
Distinguish taqyid from takhsis
Taqyid removes generality or absoluteness in any way, while takhsis specifically removes generality from a universal. For example, 'man is a species' involves takhsis, while 'a believing slave' involves taqyid.
The passage stresses that taqyid is broader than takhsis.
4
Apply to the example 'rāmi al-ḥijāra'
According to al-Razi, 'rāmi' indicates throwing attributed to something, and 'al-ḥijāra' indicates the specific body. Their combination gives the meaning of the compound, including the compositional form.
Al-ʿIṣām objected that 'rāmi' should be analyzed as indicating a relationship to a thing, not a subject. ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm defended al-Razi.
5
Recognize non-taqyidi compounds
Not all compounds are taqyidi. For instance, the passage mentions that some compounds like 'lābin' and 'tāmir' are non-taqyidi because they indicate a thing attributed to milk/dates, not qualified by them.

(قَوْلُهُ : قَيْدَاً لِلْأَوَّلِ) أي: مخرجاً لهُ عَنِ الشَّيوع والإطلاق بوجه من الوجوه، فالتَّقييدُ يُقابلُ الشُّيوع والإطلاق، بخلافِ التَّخصيص ; فإِنَّهُ يُقابل العموم فيدخلُ فيهِ مثل قولنا : الإنسانُ نوعٌ، فإنَّ الإنسان وإنْ كانَ شائعاً بين المسمى والأفراد; فقد أُخرِجَ مِن هذا الشُّيوع وقُيَّدَ بِمَا تختص بالمسمَّى ، ورقبةٌ مُؤْمِنَةٌ فَإِنَّهَا وإِنْ كَانَت شائعةٌ بينَ الرِّقَابِ المؤمنة وغيرِها ; فقد أُخرِجَت مِنَ الشَّيوع بوجه ما ، ويدخلُ فيهِ أيضاً مثلُ : جرد قطيفة، وإخلاقُ ثياب، وعَمْراً ضربتُ ، وراكباً جاءَ بكر وغيرُها ممَّا قُدِّمَ فيه القيد على المقيَّدِ لأنَّ المراد بالأوَّلِ وبالثَّاني في قولهم : إِنْ كَانَ الثَّاني قيداً لِلأَوَّلِ ; الأَوَّلُ والثَّاني رتبةٌ وتلك القيودُ مُتقدّمةً لفظاً مُتأخّرة رتبة، كذا في الخلخالي على الدَّوَّاني، قالَ أبو الفتح : ومِن هَهُنا تعلمُ أنَّ ما اشتهر مِن حَصْرِ المركَبِ التَّقييدي في الإضافي والتّوصيفي منقوض بأمثال هذه المركباتِ التَّقييديَّةِ. (قَوْلُهُ : كَرَامِي الْحِجَارَةِ) قالَ الرَّازِيُّ في شرح الأصلِ : فإنّ الرَّامِي مَقصودُ الدَّلالةِ على رمي منسوب إلى موضوع ما ، والحجارة مقصودةُ الدَّلالة على الجسمِ المعيَّنِ، ومجموع المعنيين معنى رامي الحجارة. واعترضه العصام في شرح الوضعية بأنَّ الأَوْلَى أنْ يقول إلى ذاتِ ما نسب إليهِ الرَّمْي ; لأنَّ الصَّفاتِ تعتبر فيها النسبةُ مِن جانبِ الذَّاتِ، وفي الأفعال من جانب الحدثِ. وأجابَ عبد الحكيمِ بأنَّ مَعنى كلامِ الرَّازِيِّ أنَّ الغرض منه تلك الدَّلالة، وأما قوله إلى موضوعِ مَا ; أَيْ : ذات مَا قائمُ بِهِ الرَّمْيُّ ، فالقيام أيضاً مدلولٌ له ، واحترز عن نحو لابن وتامر ; فإنَّهُ دال على ذاتِ مَا يَنسبُ إِليهِ اللَّبَنُ والتَّمرُ ; لا على مَا اتَّصفَ بِهِ ، وقوله : ومجموع المعنيين معنى رامي الحجارة; أي : معناهُ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ مركَبُ، فَلَا يردُ أنَّ لهُ جُزءاً آخَرَ، أعني : الهيئة التركيبية.
Like 'thrower of stones', and 'rational animal'. (His saying: 'like 'thrower of stones'') i.e., for 'thrower' is intended to indicate throwing attributed to some subject, and 'stones' is intended to indicate the known body. Similarly, 'animal' is intended to indicate the growing, sensing, willingly moving body, and 'rational' is intended to indicate the thinker by potential. Al-ʿAṭṭār: [It is] incomplete, and a taqyīdī compound or a non-taqyīdī compound, because the names of the mentioned divisions are these compounds, and such changes in names are common in the expressions of authors; but the apparent view is that they do not conform to language. And in it [there is] that it is permissible that the mention of these words is with respect to their original linguistic meanings, not with respect to their terminological conceptual meanings, as a reminder of the reason for naming and the strength of the appropriateness between them. (His saying: 'a restrictor of the first') i.e., it brings it out from generality and absoluteness in some way. For restriction (taqyīd) is the opposite of generality and absoluteness, unlike specification (takhṣīṣ), for it is the opposite of generality, so it includes examples like our saying 'man is a species', for 'man', although it is common between the named [i.e., the species] and individuals, it is brought out from this generality and restricted by what is specific to the named. And 'a believing slave', for it, although it is common between believing and non-believing slaves, it is brought out from generality in some way. And it includes also examples like 'a plucked velvet', 'worn clothes', 'I hit ʿAmr', 'a rider who came to Bakr', and others where the restrictor is placed before the restricted, because what is meant by 'the first' and 'the second' in their saying 'if the second is a restrictor of the first' is first and second in rank, and those restrictors are advanced in utterance but delayed in rank. Thus in al-Khalkhālī on al-Dawwānī. Abū al-Fatḥ said: From here you know that the famous limitation of taqyīdī compound to the genitive and descriptive [compounds] is refuted by examples like these taqyīdī compounds. (His saying: 'like 'thrower of stones'') Al-Rāzī said in his commentary on the original: 'for 'thrower' is intended to indicate throwing attributed to some subject, and 'stones' is intended to indicate the specific body, and the sum of the two meanings is the meaning of 'thrower of stones'.' Al-ʿIṣām objected in his commentary on al-Waḍʿiyya that it is better to say 'to a thing to which the throwing is attributed', because attributes involve the relation from the side of the essence, and in verbs from the side of the event. ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm replied that the meaning of al-Rāzī's statement is that the purpose is that indication; as for his saying 'to some subject', i.e., a thing in which the throwing inheres, so the inherence is also indicated by it. And he avoided examples like 'lābin' and 'tāmir', for they indicate a thing to which milk and dates are attributed, not what is qualified by them. And his saying 'and the sum of the two meanings is the meaning of 'thrower of stones'' i.e., its meaning inasmuch as it is compound, so it is not objected that it has another part, namely the compositional form.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of compound expressions. It begins with the example 'rāmi al-ḥijāra' (thrower of stones) and explains that both parts indicate a part of the meaning. The first part 'rāmi' indicates throwing attributed to something, and 'al-ḥijāra' indicates the specific object. Together they form the meaning. The text then distinguishes between taqyidi compound (where the second part restricts the first) and non-taqyidi compound. It gives examples like 'insānun naw'un' (man is a species) and 'raqabatun mu'minatun' (a believing slave). The passage also addresses an objection by al-'Isam against al-Razi's analysis, and a response by 'Abd al-Ḥakīm. Overall, this passage clarifies the nature of taqyidi compounds and defends the standard analysis.

Key Terms
مركب تقييدي (murakkab taqyīdī): A compound where the second part restricts the first, removing its generality.
تقييد (taqyīd): Restriction that removes generality or absoluteness in some way, contrasted with takhṣīṣ (specification) which removes generality from a universal.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Specification that removes generality from a universal, a subset of taqyīd.

C) The specific stones being thrown.

Key Takeaway
A taqyidi compound is defined by the restrictive function of its second part, a concept broader than takhsis and essential for precise definition in Islamic sciences.

Distinguishing Mufrad and Murakkab
Chapter on expressions: defines mufrad and murakkab with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mufrad from murakkab according to the logical definition and apply it to any Arabic expression.

Core Idea
Mufrad is not about word length but about whether parts indicate parts of the meaning.

In this chapter, the author establishes the foundational distinction between single words (mufrad) and compounds (murakkab). This distinction is crucial for all subsequent logical analysis, because definitions and propositions are built from expressions. The passage defines mufrad negatively: a word whose parts are not intended to indicate parts of the meaning. The commentary by al-Dassuqi clarifies the types of compounds and explains the logical structure of the definition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical definition
The definition of mufrad is: a word where no part of it is intended to indicate a part of the intended meaning. This means that if any part of the word (like a syllable or a word within a compound) independently points to a component of the overall meaning, the expression is murakkab. Memorize this criterion.
The definition is negative: 'if it is not intended...'
2
Identify the parts of the expression
Break down the Arabic expression into its smallest meaningful parts. For example, 'fī al-dār' consists of two parts: 'fī' and 'al-dār'. Each part carries a distinct meaning that contributes to the whole. In contrast, 'Zayd' has no meaningful subparts in this sense.
Parts can be words, but also morphemes. The criterion is about intention in the speech act.
3
Apply the intention test
Ask: Does the speaker intend a part of the expression to indicate a part of the meaning? If yes, it is murakkab. For example, in 'qad qāma' (he has stood), 'qad' indicates a temporal nuance and 'qāma' indicates the action. In 'Rāmi al-ḥijāra' (stone thrower), each word contributes to the meaning. If no, it is mufrad.
Proper names like 'Abdullah' are mufrad despite having two words, because the parts are not meant to indicate separate components of the meaning.
4
Verify with examples from the passage
The passage gives explicit compounds: 'fī al-dār' (noun + particle) and 'qad qāma' (verb + particle). These are murakkab. The single word 'Zayd' (from the quiz) is mufrad. Test additional expressions to solidify the distinction.
Al-Dassuqi clarifies that 'adāt' means particle (ḥarf) and 'kalima' means verb (fiʿl).

فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ وهو العمدة في باب التَّصوراتِ. (أَوْ غَيْرُهُ) إِن لم يكنِ الثَّاني قيداً للأوَّل، كالمركَّب من اسم وأداة أو كلمة وأداة. [ تعريف اللفظ المفرد] (وَإِلَّا)؛ أي: وإن لم يُقصد بجزءٍ مِنَ اللَّفظِ الدَّلالة على جزء المعنى المقصودِ ; (فَمُفْرَدٌ) الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : كَالْمُرَكَّبِ مِن اِسْمِ وَأَدَاةٍ) أي : حَرْف واسم نحو : في الدار، وقوله : (أو) كلمة) أي : فِعْل وأداةٍ نحو : قد قامَ ، فظهر أنَّ المراد بالأداة الحرفُ ، وَبِالكلمةِ الفِعْل . (قَوْلُهُ : وَإِنْ لَمْ يُقْصَدْ ...) سالبةٌ تصدق بنفي الموضوع؛ أي : تصدقُ مع نفيه.
Chapter: On Topics of Expressions, and it is the mainstay in the chapter of concepts. (Or other) if the second is not a restrictor of the first, like the compound of a noun and a particle or a verb and a particle. [Definition of the single word] (Otherwise) i.e., if it is not intended by a part of the word to indicate a part of the intended meaning, then it is single. Al-Dassuqi: His saying: 'like the compound of a noun and a particle' means a letter (ḥarf) and a noun, like 'fī al-dār', and his saying: 'or a verb' means a verb and a particle, like 'qad qāma'. So it becomes clear that by 'particle' (adāt) is meant 'letter' (ḥarf), and by 'verbal' (kalima) is meant 'verb' (fiʿl). His saying: 'and if it is not intended...' is a negative that is true by the negation of the subject; i.e., true with its negation.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on expressions (alfāẓ), which the author describes as the mainstay in the topic of concepts (taṣawwurāt). It defines the key distinction between the single word (mufrad) and the compound (murakkab). A word is mufrad if no part of it is intended to indicate a part of the meaning. If a part does indicate a part of the meaning, it is murakkab. The commentary by al-Dassuqi provides examples: a compound of a noun and a particle like 'fī al-dār' (in the house), and a verb and a particle like 'qad qāma' (he has stood). The particle is identified as ḥarf, and the verb as fiʿl. The commentary also clarifies the logical form of the definition: the condition 'if it is not intended' is a negative that is true even when the subject is negated. This is a standard logical definition.

Key Terms
مفرد (mufrad): A word no part of which is intended to indicate a part of the intended meaning. [Note: This definition is standard across the tradition.]
مركب (murakkab): A word where a part is intended to indicate a part of the meaning, or the opposite of mufrad.
أداة (adāt): In this context, a particle (ḥarf) as opposed to a noun or verb. [Note: In Arabic grammar, adāt often means a tool or particle; here it is specifically the harf.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The distinction between mufrad and murakkab is based on whether any part of the expression is intended to indicate a part of the meaning, not on the length of the expression.

Distinguishing Mufrad from Murakkab Expressions
Author defines mufrad and murakkab, listing four examples of mufrad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any Arabic expression as mufrad or murakkab according to the logical definition provided by the author, using the four examples as criteria.

Core Idea
An expression is atomic (mufrad) if no part of it is intended to signify a part of the intended meaning.

In the Islamic logical tradition, expressions are divided into atomic (mufrad) and compound (murakkab). This distinction is foundational for understanding definitions and arguments. In this lesson, we examine the precise definition given by the author and work through the four examples he provides to clarify the conditions that make an expression atomic.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition of mufrad
Locate the part of the passage that states the condition for mufrad: 'If no part of the expression is intended to signify a part of the intended meaning'. Write it down in your own words.
2
Identify the four conditions negated
The commentator points out that the four examples correlate to negating different aspects: absence of a part, absence of signification, absence of signifying the intended meaning, and absence of intending the signification. Understand how each example misses a different condition.
3
Classify each example
For each example (hamzah, Zayd, 'Abd Allah as proper noun, al-hayawan al-natiq as proper noun), explain which condition of compound is absent, and why it qualifies as mufrad.
Note that for 'Abd Allah, though it has two parts, when used as a proper noun the parts are not intended to signify separately.
4
Apply the definition to a new expression
Given the expression 'qad qama' (he has stood), determine whether it is mufrad or murakkab, and justify your answer using the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ. وهو العمدة في باب التصورات. (أو غيره) إن لم يكن الثاني قيداً للأول، كالمركب من اسم وأداة أو كلمة وأداة. (وإلا)؛ أي: وإن لم يقصد بجزء من اللفظ الدلالة على جزء المعنى المقصود؛ (فمفرد). كـ: همزة الاستفهام، وزيد، وعبد الله، والحيوان الناطق علمين.
Section: On the investigations of expressions. It is the mainstay in the chapter of concepts. (Or other) if the second is not a qualification of the first, like a compound of a noun and a particle, or a verb and a particle. (Otherwise)—i.e., if no part of the expression is intended to signify a part of the intended meaning—(then it is single). Examples: the interrogative hamzah, Zayd, 'Abd Allah, and al-hayawan al-natiq as proper nouns.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage defines the two primary divisions of expressions: compound (murakkab) and single (mufrad). The compound is when one part qualifies another, as in 'fi al-dar' (in the house) or 'qad qama' (he has stood). The single expression is when no part is intended to signify a part of the intended meaning. The four examples illustrate different ways an expression can be single: a particle alone (hamzah), a simple noun (Zayd), a compound used as a proper noun ('Abd Allah, where the parts 'abd' and 'Allah' are not intended to separately signify in this usage), and a descriptive phrase used as a proper noun (al-hayawan al-natiq as a name for a specific creature, not as a description). The examples correlate to negating different conditions of compound: absence of a part, absence of signification, absence of signifying the intended meaning, and absence of intending the signification.

Key Terms
مفرد (mufrad): An expression no part of which is intended to signify any part of the intended meaning. [Note: No significant shift.]
مركب (murakkab): An expression in which one part qualifies another, giving a composite meaning. [Note: In later texts, murakkab may include more complex structures, but the core definition remains consistent.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) عبد الله (as a proper noun)

Key Takeaway
The key insight is that mufrad status depends not on the number of parts but on whether the parts are intended to independently signify the intended meaning.

The Four Types of Simple Term and Defending Against Objections
Commentator defines the simple term and enumerates its four types, then defends against an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given Arabic term into one of the four divisions of mufrad based on the presence and intention of its parts' indications, and defend that classification against objections by distinguishing between linguistic and conventional indication.

Core Idea
The simplicity of a term depends on the linguistic intention behind its parts, not on whether it has parts.

In this passage, the commentator defines the simple term (mufrad) and lists its four divisions. He then anticipates a likely objection concerning the numerical values of letters and shows why it does not affect the classification. This lesson will help you understand how logicians categorize expressions and how they defend their categories using precise distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its parts
Determine whether the term has any parts (e.g., letters or meaningful components). For instance, 'Zayd' has three letters; 'Abdullah' has two meaningful parts: 'abd' and 'Allah'.
Parts here are the smallest units of the word, not necessarily letters if they carry meaning.
2
Check if parts have linguistic indication
Do the parts, according to the language-setter (wāḍiʿ al-lugha), indicate any meaning? For 'Zayd', the letters individually have no meaning. For 'Abdullah', 'abd' means 'slave' and 'Allah' is a proper name of God.
Ignore numerical or symbolic indications; only the original linguistic convention matters.
3
Classify into one of four divisions
Apply the four-fold scheme: (1) no parts, (2) parts but no indication, (3) parts with indication not part of the whole's intended meaning, (4) parts with indication that is part of the intended meaning but not intended when used as a proper noun.
For proper nouns like 'Zayd', it falls into division 2. For 'Abdullah' as a proper name, it falls into division 3.
4
Test against the objection
Consider the objection: letters of 'Zayd' have numerical values (Zay=7, Ya=10, Dal=4), so they do indicate. Respond by distinguishing linguistic indication from conventional number-indication.
Only the language-setter's convention matters for mufrad classification.

فصل: في مباحث الألفاظ. فالمفرد أربعة أقسام: ما لا جزء له أصلاً، وما له جزء لا دلالة له، وما له جزء يدل على غير جزء المعنى المقصود، وما له جزء يدل على جزء المعنى المقصود لكن دلالته عليه غير مقصودة. إن قلت: لا نسلم أن جزء زيد لا دلالة له أصلاً؛ لأن الزاي تدل على سبعة بالجمل، والياء تدل على عشرة، والدال تدل على أربعة؛ قلت: المعتبر الدلالة الجارية على قانون واضع اللغة، ودلالة الحروف على العدد المذكور اصطلاح لعلماء الحرف، لا لأصل اللغة.
Chapter: On Researches concerning Expressions. The simple term is of four divisions: that which has no part at all, that which has a part with no indication, that which has a part indicating something other than the intended part of the meaning, and that which has a part indicating the intended part of the meaning but its indication is not intended. If you say: We do not accept that the part of Zayd has no indication at all, because the letter Zāy indicates seven by the abjad numerals, the Yā indicates ten, and the Dāl indicates four; I say: The consideration is indication according to the convention of the language-setter, and the indication of letters to the mentioned numbers is a convention of the letter-scholars, not of the original language.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage defines the simple term (mufrad) and enumerates its four divisions according to the logicians. The commentator opens with a heading "On Researches concerning Expressions" and then states that the simple term has four divisions. The first is that which has no part at all, like a single letter hamzat al-istifhām. The second is that which has parts but none of them have any linguistic indication, like the proper noun 'Zayd' — its letters do not indicate any meaning in the language. The third is that which has parts that indicate meanings, but those meanings are not part of the intended meaning of the compound, like 'Abdullah' as a proper noun: the parts 'abd' and 'Allah' each have meaning, but the intended proper meaning (the person) is not composed of those meanings. The fourth is that which has parts that indicate meanings that are part of the intended meaning, but that indication is not intended for the definition of the compound, like 'al-ḥayawān al-nāṭiq' as a proper noun: the parts indicate 'animal' and 'rational', but the proper meaning is not that composite meaning. An objection is then raised: The letters of Zayd do have indication because each letter corresponds to a numerical value in the abjad system. The response distinguishes between linguistic indication (wadʿ al-lugha) and conventional numerical indication (iṣṭilāḥ ʿulamāʾ al-ḥarf). The only indication that matters for the definition of mufrad is that which follows the convention of the language-setter. Since the numerical values are a separate convention, they do not affect the simple term's status. This defense preserves the integrity of the classification against a superficial objection.

Key Terms
مفرد (mufrad)
جزء (juzʾ)
دلالة (dalāla)
علم (ʿalam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The letter 'hamza' used in istifhām (interrogation).

C) The phrase 'slave of Allah' (عبد الله) used as a proper noun for a person.
D) The descriptive phrase 'speaking animal' (الحيوان الناطق) used to define man.

Key Takeaway
The four divisions of mufrad show that simplicity is a matter of intended linguistic indication, not mere length or presence of parts.

Debating Individuation: Part of the Subject Matter of 'Human Person'?
Debating whether individuation is inside or outside the subject matter of the human person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the universal quiddity (humanity) and the individuated individual in logical definitions, and identify when a property belongs to the subject matter of a proper name.

Core Idea
Individuation is part of the individual person, not the universal human.

In this passage, commentators debate whether التشخص (individuation) is part of the meaning of 'human person'. The key insight is that while the universal concept 'human' does not include individuation, the term 'Zaid' or any proper name does. This distinction is crucial for definitions in jurisprudence and theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of the intended meaning
The passage states that the human quiddity is one part and individuation is the other part of the intended meaning of 'human person'. Note the phrase 'جزء المعنى المقصود'.
The quiddity is the universal essence; individuation makes it particular.
2
Understand Yasin's objection
Yasin argues that if the compound term is a proper name, its parts do not indicate parts of the meaning. He also claims individuation is outside the subject matter based on the species discussion.
This objection challenges the idea that the parts of a proper name correspond to parts of the definition.
3
Analyze al-Attar's resolution
Al-Attar concedes that individuation is outside the universal quiddity but insists it is part of the individual person. He distinguishes between the universal concept (species) and the external individual.
The resolution hinges on the difference between the shared nature and the unique individual.
4
Apply to an example from fiqh
Consider the term 'Zaid'. The universal quiddity 'human' gives generic rulings (e.g., human dignity), but individuation determines specific obligations (e.g., Zaid's wealth, age). Test with a real ruling: Zaid must pay zakat because he is a human (universal) and has wealth (individuation).
The ruling applies to the individual, not to the universal concept alone.

والماهية الإنسانية جزء المعنى المقصودِ الَّذي هو المعنى المقصودِ الَّذي هو الشَّخصُ الإنساني . فالحيوان دال على جزء المعنى المقصود؛ لأنَّ جزء الجزء جزء، الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : الشَّخْصُ الْإِنْسَانِيُّ) أي : المنسوبُ لِلإنسان؛ لكونه جزأه؛ لأنَّ الشَّخصَ الماهيَّةُ مع المشخّصات . (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى جُزْءِ الْمَعْنَى الْمَقْصُوْدِ أي: والجزء الآخر التَشخُص، هذا مُراده، وفيه نَظَر ؛ لأنَّ التَشخُص خارج عن الموضوع لهُ كَمَا سيأتي في بحثِ النَّوعِ . اهـ . ياسين . وهذا وجه أمرِهِ بالتّأمُّل، ولعلَّ وجهَهُ أيضاً : أنَّ الحيوان الناطق إذا كان عَلَماً ؛ لا يدلُّ جزؤُهُ على جزء المعنى أصلاً، وفي كلام ياسين نظر؛ لأنَّا لَا نُسلّمُ أَنَّ التَشخُصَ خارج عن الموضوع له ، نعم هو خارج عن الماهية الإنسانية كما سيأتي، وهذا لا ينافي أنَّه جزءٌ مِنَ الموضوع له، وهو الشَّخصُ الإنساني. (قَوْلُهُ: لِأَنَّ جُزْءً) وهو حيوان، وقوله : (الجزء) أي: الماهية الإنسانية، وقوله : (جزء)؛ أي: للمعنى المقصود. العطار المراد إنَّه بقي قسمان من أقسام المفردِ في الواقع وإِنْ لم يكونا دَاخِلَيْنِ تحتَ نفي القيود المذكورة؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : هي ثلاثةٌ؛ لا اثنانِ كَمَا عَدَّهَا أبو الفتح. (قَوْلُهُ: وَالْمَاهِيَّةُ الإِنْسَانِيَّةُ جُزْءُ المَعْنَى الْمَقْصُوْدِ) أي: والجزء الآخَرُ النَّشخُصُ، وَمَا في المحقِّي من التنظير بأنَّ التَّشخص خارجٌ عَنِ الموضوعِ لَهُ لِمَا سيأتي في بحثِ النَّوع أنَّهُ تَمَامُ الحقيقةِ ؛ مَدفوع بأنَّ الَّذِي يَأْتِي فِي النَّوعَ هَوَ أَنَّ التّشخُصَ خارجٌ عَن حقيقةِ الفردِ المشترك بينه وبين سائر الأفراد المشتركة معه في الحقيقةِ النَّوعيَّةِ ، والشَّخصُ هُنَا مُجُعِلَ جزءاً مِنَ الهويَّةِ المسماةِ بِذلِكَ، وهِيَ الماهيَّةُ معَ التّشخُصِ، أعني : الفرد الخارجي، والحاصِلُ أَنَّ كَوْنَ التَشخُصِ ليسَ جزءاً مِنْ ماهية المفهوم الكُلّيّ الذي هو النَّوعُ ؛ لا يُنافي كونهُ جُزءاً مِن ماهِيَّةِ الشَّخص، وقد ذكر عبد الحكيم عند الكلام على مبحثِ النَّوعِ أَنَّ التَشخُصَ عَارِضٌ للنَّوعِ ؛ نِسبتُهُ إليه نسبةَ الفَصْل إلى الجنسِ ؛ جزء للشَّخْصِ .
And the human quiddity is part of the intended meaning which is the human person. Thus 'animal' indicates part of the intended meaning because part of a part is part. al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'the human person') i.e. attributed to the human because he is a part of him; because the person is the quiddity with individuators. (His statement: 'part of the intended meaning') i.e. the other part is individuation; this is his intended meaning, but there is consideration because individuation is outside the subject matter as will come in the discussion of species. Yasin: This is why he ordered reflection; perhaps also because if 'rational animal' is a proper name, its part does not indicate part of the meaning at all. In Yasin's speech there is consideration because we do not accept that individuation is outside the subject matter; yes, it is outside the human quiddity as will come, but this does not negate that it is a part of the subject matter, which is the human person. (His statement: 'because a part') namely animal, and his statement 'the part' i.e. the human quiddity, and his statement 'part' i.e. of the intended meaning. al-Attar: What is meant is that there remain two divisions of the single word in reality even if they are not included under the negation of the mentioned restrictions; because we say they are three, not two as Abu al-Fath counted. (His statement: 'The human quiddity is part of the intended meaning') i.e. the other part is individuation. What is in the commentator's objection that individuation is outside the subject matter because what will come in the discussion of species is that it is the complete reality; is repelled by the fact that what comes in species is that individuation is outside the reality of the individual shared between it and other individuals sharing with it in the specific reality, and the person here is made part of the identity named by that, which is the quiddity with individuation, i.e. the external individual. The result is that individuation's not being part of the quiddity of the universal concept which is the species does not negate its being part of the quiddity of the person. And Abd al-Hakim mentioned in the discussion of species that individuation is an accident of the species, its relation to it is like the relation of differentia to genus, a part of the person.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange over the status of التشخص (individuation) in the definition of the human person. The original statement claims that the human quiddity is part of the intended meaning, implying that the other part is individuation. al-Dasuqi's gloss clarifies that 'human person' means the quiddity plus individuators. Yasin raises an objection: if 'rational animal' becomes a proper name (علم), then its parts do not indicate parts of the meaning at all, so the animal part no longer indicates the animality part. But al-Attar defends the original position: individuation is not part of the universal concept (species) but it is part of the external individual (person). He uses examples from fiqh: the ruling on a specific person is based on both quiddity and individuation. The key logical point: the universal concept (human) is shared, but the individual person (Zaid) includes individuation, so a part of the subject matter is the shared quiddity and a part is the unique individuation. The passage thus refines the relationship between universal and particular in definition.

Key Terms
التشخص (al-tashakhkhus): Individuation; the property that makes a universal concept a particular individual, considered part of the subject matter of the individual person but not part of the universal quiddity. [Note: In later logic, التشخص is often discussed in the context of the universals and the type-species distinction; here it is debated whether it is part of the subject of a proper name.]
الماهية الإنسانية (al-mahiyya al-insaniyya): The human quiddity; the essence of humanity considered as a universal concept, which is part of the intended meaning of the term 'human person'. [Note: Stable term across logic: refers to the essence of humanity.]
جزء المعنى المقصود (juz' al-ma'na al-maqsud): Part of the intended meaning; the quiddity is one part, and individuation is the other part, together constituting the subject matter of the term 'human person'. [Note: This usage is specific to the discussion of proper names and whether parts of a compound name still indicate parts of the meaning.]

Individuation is part of the reality of the external individual but not part of the universal quiddity; this distinction is vital for precise definitions in Islamic logic and jurisprudence.

The Logical Definition of Kalimah (Word)
Commentator defines kalimah with conditions of indicating time through form, addressing objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the logical definition of kalimah and identify its key components: indication of time through form.

Core Idea
A word in logic is defined by its form indicating time, not by its part of speech.

In logic, the term 'kalimah' has a precise meaning: it refers to an expression that indicates one of the three times (past, present, future) through its form (hay'ah/sīghah). This lesson unpacks that definition, distinguishes it from the grammatical verb, and shows how it applies to Arabic examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined: كَلِمَة (kalimah). Note that it is defined within the section on investigations of words (مباحث الألفاظ).
The logical definition differs from the grammatical definition.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The definition states: it indicates one of the three times (الماضي, الحال, المستقبل) by its configuration (هيئة) or form (صيغة). The genus is 'expression' (لفظ), implied by being a word. The differentia is the time indication via form.
The form includes the order and vocalization of letters.
3
Understand the condition of derivation
The form must arise from a derived root (مادة متصرفة), not from a non-derived radical like 'hajar'. This condition excludes words that happen to have a verb form but do not indicate time.
Examples: 'daraba' indicates past time; 'hajar' does not.
4
Compare with grammatical term
Logicians call such expressions 'kalimah', while grammarians call them 'fi'l' (verb). The passage notes this equivalence.
This shows how technical terms can cross disciplines with different scopes.
5
Apply the definition
Test examples: 'ni'ma' is included because it originally indicated time (by original position), even though it seems stripped of time. 'Ta'allam' as imperative indicates future time.
The passage addresses exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ. وصيغته عَلَى أَحَدِ الأَزْمِنَةِ الثَّلاثة كَلِمَةٌ)، وعند النحاة : فِعْل. وأجِيبُ : بأنَّ قولَهُ : فَمَعَ الدَّلالةِ ؛ أي: بأصل الوضع، والمضارع بأصل الوضع إنَّما يدلُّ على أحدِهِمَا ؛ لأنَّهُ وضع للحالِ وَلِلاستقبالِ بوضع، وبهذا الجوابِ دخل في الكلمة الأفعالُ الإنشائيَّةُ المنسلخةُ عن الزَّمانِ كنِعْمَ، وَبِئْسَ ، وعَسَى، وَلَيْسَ . (قَوْلُهُ : وَصِيغَتِهِ) عطفُ تفسير ؛ أي: صيغته الحاصلة للحروف بسبب الحركة والشكون، وتقديمُ بعض الحروفِ على بعض، وتأخير بعض الحروفِ عن بعض، قالَ قطبُ الدِّينِ الرَّازِيُّ : والمراد بالهيئة والصيغة : الهيئة الحاصلة للحروف باعتبار تقديمها وتأخيرها، وحركاتها وسكناتها، وهي صورة الكلمة (قَوْلُهُ : كَلِمَةٌ) يدخل فيها أسماء الأفعال ؛ باعتبار أنَّ الدَّلالةَ على الزَّمانِ بهيئتِهَا أعمُّ مِنْ أن يكون بواسطة أم لا، وهو ما في شرح المطالع. (قَوْلُهُ : بِهَيْئَتِهِ وَصِيْغَتِهِ) أي : بشرط أنْ يكونَ في مادَّةٍ موضوعِةٍ مُتصرَّفٍ فيها ، فلا يردُّ نحو جسق وحجر، فإنَّهما على هيئة ضرب مع عدم دلالتهما على الزَّمانِ، وللتنبيه على ذلك ؛ قالَ : ( بهيئتِهِ) ، ولم يَقُلْ : هيئة، ثمَّ إِنَّ عَطْفَ الصّيغة على الهيئةِ لِلتَّفسِيرِ ؛ لِشُهريه في المعنى المراد، والمرادُ بِهَا : الهيئة الحاصلةُ لِلحروفِ الأصولِ باعتبارِ تقديمها وتأخيرها وحركاتها وسَكَنَاتِهَا ؛ لا على الآخرِ ؛ لأنَّهُ لا اعتدادَ بِمَا يعرضُ للآخَرِ ؛ حتَّى إِنَّهُ يجعلُ تعلَّمْ وَتَعَلَّمَ أمراً وماضياً على هيئةٍ واحدةٍ، ثمَّ المرادُ الدَّلالةُ بحسب الوضع لتخرج الأفعالُ المنسلِخَةُ عَنِ الزَّمانِ، قال المصنِّفُ : ودَلالة الكلمة على الزَّمَانِ بِالصِّيغةِ إنَّما يصح في لُغَةِ العربِ دونَ لُغَةِ العجم، فإِنَّ قولَكَ : آمد وآيد؛ مُتَحدانِ في الصيغة مختلفان بالزَّمانِ مع أنَّ نظر الفنّ في الألفاظ على وجه كُلِّيِّ غيرُ مخصوص بِلُغةٍ دونَ لُغَةٍ أُخرى، وأجابَ السَّيِّدُ بِأَنَّ الاهتمامَ بِاللُّغَةِ العربيَّةِ الَّتِي دُوِّنَ بِهَا هذا الفن غالباً في زماننا أكثرَ ، ولا بُعْدَ في اختصاص بعض الأحوالِ بِهذهِ اللّغةِ ا . هـ. (قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ النُّحَاةِ فِعْلٌ) الدَّاتُ يعني أنَّ مَا يُسمَّى عند المنطقيِّينَ كَلمةٌ، بهيئته على أحدِ الأزمنةِ الثَّلاثةِ ؛ هو مَا يُسمَّى عندَ النَّحويِّينَ فِعْلاً .
A chapter: On the investigations of words. And its form upon one of the three times is a word (kalimah), and according to grammarians: a verb. And it is answered: that his statement 'fama'a al-dalalah' means: due to the original position, and the present tense verb by original position only indicates one of them; because it was positioned for the present and future by one position, and by this answer the performative verbs stripped of time such as ni'ma, bi'sa, 'asa, and laysa enter into the word. His statement: 'and its form' is an explanatory conjunction; i.e., its form arising from the letters due to movement and quiescence, and the placing of some letters before others, and the placing of some letters after others. Qutb al-Din al-Razi said: And what is meant by the configuration and form: the configuration arising from the letters by considering their precedence and delay, their movements and quiescences, and it is the image of the word. His statement: 'a word' includes verbal nouns; by considering that the indication of time by its configuration is more general than being by means or not, and this is in Sharh al-Matali'. His statement: 'by its configuration and form' means: on condition that it be in a subject matter that is disposed (mutasarrif), so that examples like 'jasq' and 'hajar' are not excluded, for they are on the configuration of 'daraba' while not indicating time, and to alert to that he said: 'by its configuration', and did not say 'a configuration', then indeed the coordinating conjunction of 'form' to 'configuration' is for explanation; due to its fame in the intended meaning. And what is meant by it: the configuration arising from the root letters by considering their precedence and delay, their movements and quiescences; not upon the extra ones; because no attention is given to what occurs to the extra; so that he makes 'ta'allam' and 'ta'allama' as imperative and past on one configuration. Then what is meant is the indication according to position in order to exclude the verbs stripped of time. The author said: The indication of the word for time by the form is only valid in the Arabic language, not in the language of non-Arabs, for your saying 'āmed' and 'āyed' are identical in form but differ in time, while the consideration of the art regarding words is universal, not specific to one language over another. And al-Sayyid answered that the attention to the Arabic language, in which this art has been compiled mostly in our time, is greater, and there is no impossibility in specifying some states to this language. His statement: 'and according to grammarians: a verb' means that what is called by logicians a word, by its configuration upon one of the three times, is what is called by grammarians a verb.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage defines the logical term 'kalimah' (word) and distinguishes it from the grammatical 'verb'. The author begins by stating the definition: a word is a linguistic expression that indicates one of the three times (past, present, future) through its form (hay'ah) or shape (sīghah). This is said to be termed 'verb' by grammarians. The commentary then addresses objections. First, it defends the inclusion of certain performative verbs (like ni'ma, bi'sa) that seem to lack time by explaining that the condition of indicating time is by original position (asl al-wad‘), and such verbs were originally placed for a time. Second, it clarifies that 'by its form' means the configuration of the root letters with their movements and order, excluding non-derived words like 'jasq' which have the same form but do not indicate time. Third, it notes that this definition applies to Arabic by default, as most logical works are in Arabic, though the principles are universal. The passage thus refines the logical definition of a word, ensuring it includes derived verbal nouns and excludes non-derived radicals, while addressing cross-linguistic concerns.

Key Terms
كَلِمَةٌ (kalimah): A word that indicates one of the three times (past, present, future) through its form (hay'ah) or shape (sīghah), according to logicians. [Note: In Arabic grammar, kalimah can mean any word, but here it is restricted to verb-like words indicating time.]
هَيْئَة (hay'ah): The configuration of letters by their order, movements, and quiescences, which gives the form of the word.
صِيغَة (sīghah): Synonymous with hay'ah in this context, explained as the form arising from the root letters' order and vocalization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the logical definition, which of the following is NOT considered a kalimah?
A) 'daraba' (ضرب) indicating past time
B) 'ni'ma' (نعم) indicating praise
C) 'hajar' (حجر) a stone
D) 'ta'allam' (تعلم) imperative

Key Takeaway
The logical definition of kalimah hinges on form indicating time; non-derived radicals and words stripped of time are excluded.

Conditions and Exceptions for Time Indication in Kalimah
Commentator defines kalimah with conditions of indicating time through form, addressing objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of derivation (mutasarrif) and original position (asl al-wad‘) to determine if an Arabic expression is a kalimah.

Core Idea
The time indication must be by original position, not by circumstance.

The definition of kalimah includes a crucial condition: the word's form must arise from a derived root that is mutasarrif. This lesson explores this condition, as well as the exception for performative verbs that seem to lack time but are included because they originally indicated time by position.

Guided Path
1
Learn the condition 'mutasarrif'
The word must be derived from a root that undergoes inflection; non-derived radicals like 'hajar' are excluded even if they look like a verb form.
This prevents false positives.
2
Understand 'asl al-wad‘'
The present tense verb (مضارع) was placed for both present and future by one position. Thus, it indicates one of the two, not both, but by original position it covers both possibilities. This answers the objection that present tense indicates two times.
This is key for including verbs like 'yadribu'.
3
Analyze performative verbs
Verbs like 'ni'ma', 'bi'sa', 'casa', 'laysa' are considered kalimah because they originally indicated time, even if in usage they seem timeless. The commentator defends their inclusion.
This shows that original position takes precedence over current usage.
4
Examine the role of extra letters
The form (hay'ah) considers only the root letters; extra letters (e.g., in 'ta'allam') do not affect the indication of time. Thus, 'ta'allam' as imperative and 'ta'allama' as past have the same root form but differ in time.
This refines what 'form' means.
5
Practice determining kalimah
Given a set of Arabic words, decide if they meet the conditions: derived root, time indication via form, not excluded by non-derivation or lack of original position.
Use examples from the passage.

فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ. وصيغته عَلَى أَحَدِ الأَزْمِنَةِ الثَّلاثة كَلِمَةٌ)، وعند النحاة : فِعْل. وأجِيبُ : بأنَّ قولَهُ : فَمَعَ الدَّلالةِ ؛ أي: بأصل الوضع، والمضارع بأصل الوضع إنَّما يدلُّ على أحدِهِمَا ؛ لأنَّهُ وضع للحالِ وَلِلاستقبالِ بوضع، وبهذا الجوابِ دخل في الكلمة الأفعالُ الإنشائيَّةُ المنسلخةُ عن الزَّمانِ كنِعْمَ، وَبِئْسَ ، وعَسَى، وَلَيْسَ . (قَوْلُهُ : وَصِيغَتِهِ) عطفُ تفسير ؛ أي: صيغته الحاصلة للحروف بسبب الحركة والشكون، وتقديمُ بعض الحروفِ على بعض، وتأخير بعض الحروفِ عن بعض، قالَ قطبُ الدِّينِ الرَّازِيُّ : والمراد بالهيئة والصيغة : الهيئة الحاصلة للحروف باعتبار تقديمها وتأخيرها، وحركاتها وسكناتها، وهي صورة الكلمة (قَوْلُهُ : كَلِمَةٌ) يدخل فيها أسماء الأفعال ؛ باعتبار أنَّ الدَّلالةَ على الزَّمانِ بهيئتِهَا أعمُّ مِنْ أن يكون بواسطة أم لا، وهو ما في شرح المطالع. (قَوْلُهُ : بِهَيْئَتِهِ وَصِيْغَتِهِ) أي : بشرط أنْ يكونَ في مادَّةٍ موضوعِةٍ مُتصرَّفٍ فيها ، فلا يردُّ نحو جسق وحجر، فإنَّهما على هيئة ضرب مع عدم دلالتهما على الزَّمانِ، وللتنبيه على ذلك ؛ قالَ : ( بهيئتِهِ) ، ولم يَقُلْ : هيئة، ثمَّ إِنَّ عَطْفَ الصّيغة على الهيئةِ لِلتَّفسِيرِ ؛ لِشُهريه في المعنى المراد، والمرادُ بِهَا : الهيئة الحاصلةُ لِلحروفِ الأصولِ باعتبارِ تقديمها وتأخيرها وحركاتها وسَكَنَاتِهَا ؛ لا على الآخرِ ؛ لأنَّهُ لا اعتدادَ بِمَا يعرضُ للآخَرِ ؛ حتَّى إِنَّهُ يجعلُ تعلَّمْ وَتَعَلَّمَ أمراً وماضياً على هيئةٍ واحدةٍ، ثمَّ المرادُ الدَّلالةُ بحسب الوضع لتخرج الأفعالُ المنسلِخَةُ عَنِ الزَّمانِ، قال المصنِّفُ : ودَلالة الكلمة على الزَّمَانِ بِالصِّيغةِ إنَّما يصح في لُغَةِ العربِ دونَ لُغَةِ العجم، فإِنَّ قولَكَ : آمد وآيد؛ مُتَحدانِ في الصيغة مختلفان بالزَّمانِ مع أنَّ نظر الفنّ في الألفاظ على وجه كُلِّيِّ غيرُ مخصوص بِلُغةٍ دونَ لُغَةٍ أُخرى، وأجابَ السَّيِّدُ بِأَنَّ الاهتمامَ بِاللُّغَةِ العربيَّةِ الَّتِي دُوِّنَ بِهَا هذا الفن غالباً في زماننا أكثرَ ، ولا بُعْدَ في اختصاص بعض الأحوالِ بِهذهِ اللّغةِ ا . هـ. (قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ النُّحَاةِ فِعْلٌ) الدَّاتُ يعني أنَّ مَا يُسمَّى عند المنطقيِّينَ كَلمةٌ، بهيئته على أحدِ الأزمنةِ الثَّلاثةِ ؛ هو مَا يُسمَّى عندَ النَّحويِّينَ فِعْلاً .
A chapter: On the investigations of words. And its form upon one of the three times is a word (kalimah), and according to grammarians: a verb. And it is answered: that his statement 'fama'a al-dalalah' means: due to the original position, and the present tense verb by original position only indicates one of them; because it was positioned for the present and future by one position, and by this answer the performative verbs stripped of time such as ni'ma, bi'sa, 'asa, and laysa enter into the word. His statement: 'and its form' is an explanatory conjunction; i.e., its form arising from the letters due to movement and quiescence, and the placing of some letters before others, and the placing of some letters after others. Qutb al-Din al-Razi said: And what is meant by the configuration and form: the configuration arising from the letters by considering their precedence and delay, their movements and quiescences, and it is the image of the word. His statement: 'a word' includes verbal nouns; by considering that the indication of time by its configuration is more general than being by means or not, and this is in Sharh al-Matali'. His statement: 'by its configuration and form' means: on condition that it be in a subject matter that is disposed (mutasarrif), so that examples like 'jasq' and 'hajar' are not excluded, for they are on the configuration of 'daraba' while not indicating time, and to alert to that he said: 'by its configuration', and did not say 'a configuration', then indeed the coordinating conjunction of 'form' to 'configuration' is for explanation; due to its fame in the intended meaning. And what is meant by it: the configuration arising from the root letters by considering their precedence and delay, their movements and quiescences; not upon the extra ones; because no attention is given to what occurs to the extra; so that he makes 'ta'allam' and 'ta'allama' as imperative and past on one configuration. Then what is meant is the indication according to position in order to exclude the verbs stripped of time. The author said: The indication of the word for time by the form is only valid in the Arabic language, not in the language of non-Arabs, for your saying 'āmed' and 'āyed' are identical in form but differ in time, while the consideration of the art regarding words is universal, not specific to one language over another. And al-Sayyid answered that the attention to the Arabic language, in which this art has been compiled mostly in our time, is greater, and there is no impossibility in specifying some states to this language. His statement: 'and according to grammarians: a verb' means that what is called by logicians a word, by its configuration upon one of the three times, is what is called by grammarians a verb.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage defines the logical term 'kalimah' (word) and distinguishes it from the grammatical 'verb'. The author begins by stating the definition: a word is a linguistic expression that indicates one of the three times (past, present, future) through its form (hay'ah) or shape (sīghah). This is said to be termed 'verb' by grammarians. The commentary then addresses objections. First, it defends the inclusion of certain performative verbs (like ni'ma, bi'sa) that seem to lack time by explaining that the condition of indicating time is by original position (asl al-wad‘), and such verbs were originally placed for a time. Second, it clarifies that 'by its form' means the configuration of the root letters with their movements and order, excluding non-derived words like 'jasq' which have the same form but do not indicate time. Third, it notes that this definition applies to Arabic by default, as most logical works are in Arabic, though the principles are universal. The passage thus refines the logical definition of a word, ensuring it includes derived verbal nouns and excludes non-derived radicals, while addressing cross-linguistic concerns.

Key Terms
كَلِمَةٌ (kalimah): A word that indicates one of the three times (past, present, future) through its form (hay'ah) or shape (sīghah), according to logicians. [Note: In Arabic grammar, kalimah can mean any word, but here it is restricted to verb-like words indicating time.]
هَيْئَة (hay'ah): The configuration of letters by their order, movements, and quiescences, which gives the form of the word.
صِيغَة (sīghah): Synonymous with hay'ah in this context, explained as the form arising from the root letters' order and vocalization.

The Universal Scope of Logical Terms: Arabic and Other Languages
Commentator defines kalimah with conditions of indicating time through form, addressing objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the logical definition of kalimah is often presented for Arabic and argue for its universal applicability.

Core Idea
Logic studies words universally, but Arabic serves as the model due to tradition.

The passage notes that the definition of kalimah by form indicating time is valid for Arabic but not for other languages like Persian. This raises a question: is logic language-specific? The commentator (al-Sayyid) answers that the attention to Arabic is greater in this field, and there is no impossibility in specifying some states to Arabic. This lesson explores the universal scope of logical terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The author states that the definition only works for Arabic because in other languages, words identical in form can have different times (e.g., 'āmed' and 'āyed' in Persian). So the definition seems language-bound.
This challenges the universality of logic.
2
Understand the objection
If logic studies words in general, not specifically Arabic, then a definition that only applies to Arabic is insufficient.
The commentary addresses this.
3
Analyze al-Sayyid's answer
Al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani responds that the attention to Arabic is greater because most logical works are compiled in Arabic, especially in our time. There is no impossibility in specifying some properties to Arabic.
This is a pragmatic justification.
4
Reflect on the universal principle
The definition is not inherently language-specific; it describes a property that exists in Arabic. Other languages may have other ways to indicate time. The logical concept of 'word indicating time' is universal, but the specific means (form) varies.
The lesson is about scope and abstraction.
5
Apply to Islamic scholarship
In Islamic logic (mantiq), most examples are from Arabic because the Quran and Hadith are in Arabic. The tools are transferable, but the illustrations are language-specific.
This helps in studying logic in other languages.
